However, in one manner, you make three or four incisions, lining them up according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the liver cautery that we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient lie down on his back; and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two veins, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and remove the fat that is next to the mouse, or the incision that the patient comes towards the left side, and lift the elevations from which you remove the fat according to the direction of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After placing the two nerves inflamed, make them pierced from the other side, then pull out the fire-cautery, and thus in it will have four holes. If you see, if you cauterize the entire cautery to three holes.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After healing when it has discharged pus for a long time, and this is worth using the other remedies before mentioned.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 Fire-cautery does not work against edema, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When the cure according to the ways we have said in divisions does not work, then you must make four fire-cauteries around the boil, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the bladder, and two behind the back near the spine, and one at the worst place; and the fire-cauteries should be close to the thick part of the boil.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the fire cautery is opened to expel pus for a long time, do not neglect the care of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will come together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the clavicle as shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as it has been stated before.
de l’enfleure des piez	swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in one who is edematous, and filled with yellow pus, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and dip your hand with the cautery without turning it.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deep, as this would drive the pus forcefully, and let the cautery be shaped in such a way:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making .2 cauteries on each leg with the tip of the knife; and let the cauteries be long, one under the thigh in front and the other outside, inside the leg; and leave the cauteries above for a long time to heal, as much as possible; after curing the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the remedy
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the stomach comes from coldness and moisture, while the digestive and retentive virtues that are in the stomach and the intestine are blocked, and cannot be cured by means of treatments; and you see the patient suffering greatly and having strong symptoms, do .i. large cautery on the stomach as described earlier or cautery of the stomach, around it circulate; and .iiij. subtle cauteries around the navel, each .i. cautery clavile subtle, and .ij. cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, do cautery on the thumb, and .i. cautery on each joint, and .ij. small cauteries on the stomach around the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure for hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When hemorrhoids are founded or multiple, and they are old and filled with cold and moist corrupted humors, and have been cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not help if cauteries are done: III on the spine of the back, which is far from the coccyx and moves triangularly, and the cautery should be placed under the buttock; if you think that the stomach is cold and meat does not cook, and the face swells, then the stomach receives a large cautery as described earlier, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with the whole cautery stick; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the joint until it heals.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh-like substance called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply althelul (a substance), heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely over the althelul-applied area; let your hand remain until the cautery reaches the vein opening, so that it does not burn the skin; do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each area as we have said; afterwards, apply ointments for healing while they are healthy; and if you cauterize a large cautery over an ulcer, it will provide more help.
de plaie mal curee	of an ill-healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot bear incision or opening, we will describe the disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 When a boil comes, it is swollen and filled with pus and corrupted moisture, you must probe it entirely with a delicate test, and be aware that you know the extent of the probe to what extent it is full.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 After heating the cautery that appears to be a shaver, and push it into the boil according to the size that the probe has entered, and repeat the cautery until the body becomes burned and corrupted, once or twice, according to the quantity of pus needed; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is near, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 If the boil goes to the body of the bladder and intestines, be careful with these places, do not act outside the charnel house, consider that it is not persistent; after curing the joint until it heals, if the joint is pierced and materials have been removed for a long time, then know that the joint is healed entirely; but if the materials are not removed, know that the joint is broken, and the bone is corrupted in this way as one of those whom we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	On the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys and with great swelling, and does not take on a female form, then you must make a cautery over the kidneys on both sides with the cautery clavile as we have previously said; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be four cauteries in a row, and they will provide more help.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then you make a cautery on the part outside the bladder, where the hairs begin at the tip, one on the right and one on the left, each as long as our thumb; and you make one cautery on the other side of the back if needed, or two if necessary; and the cauteries should be as thick as a nail according to the shape mentioned above.
de la marris	Of the anus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the anus is cold and moist and does not permit conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their term ends slowly; and when they come, it causes great pain: then you must make four cauteries around the anus, as we have said in the treatment of the bladder, and two cauteries on the other side of the back; and the cauteries should be as thick as a nail, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the swelling
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends to the swelling's container and thus causes it to move out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joint is found to have moved from its proper place, then you must cauterize the patient on the swelling's container with a cautionery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the joint surrounding the container so that the container is within the circle; and if the cautery is as those who have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautionery is not present, make four large olive-oil cauteries and let them be as full as all the others; and let it heal until it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hernia
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the swelling of a hernia, and it is due to coldness or moisture, and the patient is cured of this as we have said in the division, but the cure is not worthwhile; and the disease is ancient: therefore you must purge the patient with foul-smelling pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterwards comes the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two ways: namely, with burning medications, and cautery of fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 The method of the fire cautery is according to many ways, one of which is this: you should make three triangular cauteries together on the backside of the haunch, and make it deep and wide, with space between each cauterization about the size of a thumb, and the cauteries should be olive-shaped; sometimes the cautery is made in the middle on the top of the haunch, for which there are four as such:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, use the round cautery in the circle as we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the shoulder; but do it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire shoulder, and all the edges should be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the manner in which it is done in sciatica, when the pain remains in the loin, and does not reach as far as the thigh nor the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it comes up to the thigh and leg, he shall have fire cautery where the pain is felt, and the cautery 4 fingers above the ankle, on the left side slightly; and let the cauter be with a cutting tool, and let the thickness of the coal be thinned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to 2 fingers or closer, let him cauterize there where he feels the pain 3 or 4 fingers from the heel, which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if you know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a lancet or circular shape, and be careful in all your cauterizations not to let the cautery burn nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient any greater harm or contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen many who performed a fire cautery on the ankle bone and let it stay until the leg was swollen completely and also the feet, and all the toes were pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After an abdominal solution, he had death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two places together, make a fire cautery on one and the other as follows:
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise will say for the cautery of the heel, as follows, make this iron and it should be as big as a thumbnail or slightly smaller, and it should have notches or one notch from one end to the other with the space between the notches the size of a nut; and the notches should be above two parts, and they should also be like nuts, and there should be a good heel of iron; this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heat it so that it becomes completely red and roasted, and then place it on the sick heel box, turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery rod and leave for four days; then apply a plaster of butter, and keep the wound open for a long time; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery due to its fearsome appearance, and few who use it know how to do so; but nonetheless it is a good cautery which can be borne by those who can endure it, and there where it burns.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The fire cautery of medicine is that you make the instrument inside the joint, where the margin of the door [joint] should be pierced, and it should be made of iron or steel with a long shaft, and at the top have two eyes, and between each eye have the width of a thumb; and they should be open and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 After placing the hot iron [cautery] on the patient lying on their side, and after your hand is near the hot iron [cautery]; afterwards pour hot oil between the two circles of the hot iron [cautery], which has been heated in the fire pot, and leave it for an hour; allow the patient to bear the heat and burn from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it burns like a bite from fire, and when the biting has passed, take your hand with the instrument and gently raise the swelling; leave it thus for three days, and place butter over it until the blackness of the blister is removed; leave it for three more days so that pus can drain out; and this will be the final help after ointment treatment until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has spread to the thigh or the leg, make the instrument that dyes according to what you have done on the swelling; it is the method of hot water, and I have written or treated its correction in medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take equal parts of alkali and hot live coals, grind them together, and put the mixture into a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 Have a small hole opened slightly so that the tip of a razor can enter; and put one pot on top of the other well weighed down, then add alkali and coal and water softly, until there are two inches above the powder that you have thoroughly mixed with your hand; leave it in this state until it settles down to the powder or pot breaks, then take all that settles, and pour it over coal and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it becomes very hot and is administered in the work of various medical treatments and in cauterization of other limbs, because it does similar work as fire, and if applied to a wound like this [mentioned above] with tisane and honey and coal with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure in which a man was healed from the pain of the hernia and sciatica, and highly praises it, and says that no other cure was made, and that he became healthy once when this cure was performed, and he was bathed as instructed afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says that you take green willow bark powder and mix it with a little grease, apply it to the hernia and to the thigh and leg where the pain is located and hold it; leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 Then make him enter the bath until his body is slightly warmed, and make him lie down, and the pain will disappear completely and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such fire cauterization unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Diascorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's fat, it helps much; and the cauterization should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take linen and beat it with old oil, and place it over the groove that is between the toe of the foot and the one called the phalanx.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 After taking dry goat's fat and heating it over the fire until it becomes charcoal, place it on the linen, and leave it until it cools; then do it again in this manner, and keep doing so until you think with your senses that it has reached the bone, and the pain is stopped; and this method of cauterization is called "cauterization of goat's fat.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, either from falling or striking or excessive evacuation, or from similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these symptoms are worth cauterizing except for one who suffers from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is required afterwards that the patient be emptied of fetid pills or similar things, which are placed on the back, where the pain occurs, three lines marked with ink, and in each line 5 or more cauteries according to its potency and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make 4 cauteries or 4 at the mid-sized cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrow anus when they defecate, and fear; and you find it in the lower spine of the back and in its appearance which appears above other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 The cautery burns every part of the spine enlarges.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery touching it two or three lines apart and let the tips be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After healing the place until it is healthy as we have said, be careful not to use a cautery in a place that is in nerve pain.
de la dolor des jointes	"of the pain of joints"
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	"When the pain of joints is due to moisture that spreads throughout all parts of the body, and when it comes in feet, which people call gout properly, and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make a small amount of cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:"
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary to prick the face of the foot, make the cautery touch it all along its length, as they say "without point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pain comes to the knees and other joints, which happens often, make the cautery touch each knee three or four times on each side, using an olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand away from it more than necessary until the curvature of the burning is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend to the genitals and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 If the pains are in the hands, make a puncture two lines deep; and if there is no pain in the fingers, make a puncture on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the arms or shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and consider medications.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you take good care of him and purge bile, he will be cured with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the hernia
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When worms come in wounds, and the belly swells as a result, it is necessary that when you wish to treat it, the patient should not eat anything that day; and that he uses things which relieve the stomach, so that the worms descend from his stomach; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm straight until the belly recovers, and then press down on the swelling at your sides, and press firmly on top of the wound over the bone of the elbow, and give a sign that resembles half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery as shown in this figure:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it becomes white and he expels pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then move the bowels to their place; and have the minister hold his hand so it does not return; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put the cushion and the sergeant on the thighs, and the other on the buttocks that holds the hands; then place the cautery over the sign on your whole hand, and hold it straight and as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; be careful that the bowels do not come out when you cauterize; and do not burn him; and by doing so, may the patient not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 The cautery for children should be subtle according to their size, and the same for grown-ups according to theirs; after three days, care the burn with butter until the blister is removed; afterwards, use other ointments until it heals completely, and have the patient lie on his back for forty days as long as the wound is healing well; and the exudate should be allowed to dry out, so that the pus does not protrude when he gets up to go to his room.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 After forty days, when he wants to get up, bring him a well-made mattress and let him lie on it for another forty days; have good rest, so that he does not overexert himself, and be careful of too much drinking and eating, and excessive vomiting; and if he follows this instruction, he will heal completely.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I shall say hereafter the treatment of amputation in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the hernia from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When roundworms appear in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow more, then make the fire cautery for it as per its quantity, and let it be burned one third of the belly; afterwards treat it according to what has been said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the mid-point and make a line over the roundworm, and another below it, and then hold your hand at the entire length of the fire cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the initial cauterizations are lighter and more moist.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes in any member, either from falling or being struck, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the medicine does not help, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the member, its smallness and weakness, and its virtue and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If it is healed from the first cautery, that's good; but if it starts again with another cautery on top of the previous one, because it is customary for it to change in the nearby member, so you should apply the cauteries as long as the patient is healing.
de meselerie	To mix medications
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The sick are sometimes helped by cautery with great assistance, and the same applies to diseases that come from the rotting of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 Can you see if it needs to be cauterized, take care if the patient is at the beginning, and if it has been treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not discharge or remain, and you doubt that corruption will affect the entire patient, then perform V cauteries on the head: I take hold of the head with one hand, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and II (two) on the II (two) horns, and I behind on the haiterel; and leave your hand thus that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the scabs come out from within so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize on the muscle according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the medication is scattered everywhere, it clearly perishes, then you must cauterize with the cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery on the nape of the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the calf and another below it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the legs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the veins that are above the last calcament, that you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the finger, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more you perform cautery, the more aid it provides and benefits him; and know that the sick feel no pain during cautery as the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in methods of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After curing the limb with flour of oats with honey and other treatments until it is drained.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When a swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters but is not drained, then you make cauteries on the member according to the size and smallness of the member; and the cauterization should be slightly deep into the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is drained.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes one makes a fire cauterization at the hand, foot, and back, at the nerve exit point that makes the limb numb, and thus the inflammation is removed; nevertheless, no one should interfere with it unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the movement of the nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of bandages
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" occurs and the instruments of medicine are of no use, cauterize it with a shallow cautery according to the size of the sore, until the blister is removed and its color changes; then cure it with wheat flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and goose blood and almond blood, each in equal parts; mix them all together, tie it up with a cloth, and apply it to the place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	cure of scrofula by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a boil begins and you want to stop it, if you cauterize it with a circular cautery around the entire boil.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 Nevertheless, the wise say that one should cauterize in the middle of the boil; however, this does not seem good to me because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen before; and a more correct thing is to be cauterized around it with a circular cautery, as we said earlier about cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the swelling that cannot grow
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which is slow to heal or due to its excessiveness or because the patient is aged and decrepit (meaning very old) with little blood, or due to the time; and you see it hasten to heal: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it as it is.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 Then it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced completely with fire cautery, heat the fire cautery as follows:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have penetrated the heat, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels it burning slightly to the extent that the course of the pustule is cleared.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the patient has completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	cure with fire using iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another type of disease is called "corrosion," which is nothing but an erosion of a limb, as it eats away at the limbs just like fire dries up damp wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can be treated with a fire cautery, then warm the cauteries little by little and large, according to the place or the diseased area; after the cauterization of all parts so that you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, that everything corrupted should be excised.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and place on the areas cauterized soft powder with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the cure of onions producing heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if you see after three days that healthy char does not grow, it is good; and if not, repeat the cautery on the lesion that remained corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this cautery has sometimes been cured with hot medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of hot medicine in the division: take it when needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The growing pains that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 It often happens that through the foot a disease called "closing" comes out, according to our understanding, which is a large thing clothed in the foot and bites the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries of this disease are according to two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 This is to know fire cautery and water hot cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 This is about fire cautery and water hot cautery. To perform fire cautery, heat the iron as a feather of a plowshare, made from good iron so that it can penetrate all around, and have fine edges; place the heated iron on top of the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the base of the nail; leave it for three days until pus starts to come out; then make a plaster of bitter herbs ground with oil, and leave the plaster on for the entire night, and the nail will shrivel up and be removed from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the joint with soothing ointment while it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if it has been turned outward by the body's fluids, and this often happens in hands and feet, you must apply a hot cautery. This is how: take a wire of iron or copper, or a splint made from willow, and place it on top of the nail and the sore, that is to say to prick blisters; then place the wire around it so it presses all around, next put a bit of hot oil there and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand in twisting so the edge of the wire comes to the root of the nail, allowing the hot oil to find its way deep into the root; let the patient endure a bit of the burning of the hot oil for an hour, then leave it like that, and it will rot away at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Therefore do as before, while you heat all those who are in the body, then heal them with ointments that warm flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for shaking (trembling)
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes due to coldness of the nerves, or fever of four days or other, you should make them 4 or 5 cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each spine; and one in the pelvis area, and one on the stomach with the olive-oil cautery; this will stop the shaking and hasten recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	of putrid sores (pustules)
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes the body appears bathed with sores or pus, which come from large corrupt matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 First, when they appear, it is necessary to perform a fire cautery on each head of the pus: a subtle cautioner made from myrtle wood, so that the point is taken by fire, or from the long root of aristolochia, or the lenticular cautioner.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluidities from which they come are destroyed, and they heal; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great displacements of blood from the cut artery at the wound or the abscess incision, or the member's cautery, and similar things; and it is a very bad thing to let it flow out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	However, if it happens to someone, you should hurry and put your finger on the vein wound, and press as hard as possible to stop the blood flowing out below your finger, and let no more come out; then take olive oil-soaked cauteries of various sizes and apply them until they are all red; then take .i., either large or small depending on the wound and the location in which the artery is cut, and place the cautery on the vein where you have your finger, and hold the cautery there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a jump occurs when you place your finger on the vein and the cautery is ready, take quickly another one of the cauteries that are near fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	Keep doing this one after the other until the blood stops flowing; be careful not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and take care that no other harm comes to the patient; know that when the artery bursts, it cannot be properly stopped when the arteries are large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly binding with thread, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop the blood; and bind and tighten accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the binding of a tight cloth or places something burning or similar things on it, will not help if it does not work.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no medicine present, you should place your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it remains swollen above the wound and the vein; and do not move it, but wet it with cold frequently so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and remains swollen; and proceed with the inquiry in front of those from whom you need cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases that require fire cautery or burning medicine, their causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; I placed that chapter from the head to the feet, and I will proceed with this chapter in the same way for those who find it easier to understand what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And likewise as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many kinds of people come in treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 There also come those who treat themselves so that they die quickly because of the foolishness they find with their disease, and from the greatness of its malignancy; and these should be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And among these there are those who give you their advice, saying "wait, I am cured," but the disease is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not good that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but give more thought to your honor than your desire, and do not trust foolishly but wisely from those of whom you are certain, and from which you have learned; and use prediction and indication in the treatments of your patients so that health may be turned; and this will help you acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lord grants you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Further, I have organized this chapter by speaking in chapters, following the order of each chapter of cauteries that I have previously described from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand what you need from these.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The full head is filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children during childbirth, and sometimes it happens due to reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and all that I have seen quickly dies; therefore it seems to me that I should spend less effort on these treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I have seen one child whose head was filled with water, and it grew larger every day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture gathered underneath the skull bone between the brain and the bone, and the treatments are such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a large incision in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and see here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs you see are the commissures of the head opening from each side, and the pus gushes out when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not return: then you must make four incisions within the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 And after the incision remove the dressings and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it until the fifth day; then undress it, and cure the wound with lances and ointments, and allow the swelling to decrease, and give the patient dry meat from a bird without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the abscess is at its widest, and join the watery part; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut there where the abscess opens, and the accumulated part of the watery fluid; and do as you can with it; but be careful not to damage the artery; and make sure that some blood flows out, so that the patient dies a natural death from the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of boil
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is any disease called "cataract" in the eyes or at its worst, and the disease is old and the medicine's cure does not help, then the last cure is the cautery on the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Then, when you see that it is covered, the patient should bend over his head; then rub the side of a coarse cloth on it until the arteries appear, then the patient should grasp his neck with the cloth; then look where the veins are biting, and the sides of both ears are behind them; then mark the place in the middle, then strike one and the other with a sharp spatula of two fingers deep, until the cut comes to the bone, and this should be along the wide part of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, push the spatula under the artery and cut it from above, cutting as deep as two fingers together.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, it jumps continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 If the artery does not open on its own, you must measure the space of three fingers, then press and go up to the bone; and it is required to evacuate six cubits of blood, and possibly a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains on the bone without shrinking, if the wound that was incised does not swell, then hold the wound and bind it, and treat the ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old migraine comes, and the acute catarrh, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and similar things such as an ancient fevered head, and it is treated by methods of medicines but none of them help, then we should cut open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have mentioned.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient bends back the hairs on his temples, and listens for the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well with its beating, and it is not difficult to find unless in some cold people; and if it is found, the patient should grasp its neck with some cloth, then rub the area with a harsh cloth, and moisten the area with warm water until the arteries appear clearly; then take the spatumile (a medical instrument) of this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 Then carefully cut the skin lightly so that you reach the artery, then pull it up to the clamps, and remove well the cloths that are underneath from each part; and if the artery is delicate, turn it to the tip of the scissors, then press that part according to the quantity of the two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 If it is not cut, it does not move at all in any way.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the .vj. c/, until .iij.; and if the artery is large, you must tie it with a double strong silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound closes and bleeding comes to a stop; then cut off the excess that is between the two ligatures in the same hour itself, and if you see, you cauterize the wound with the cautery until the bone is cut through; this is the amputation work, if the patient does not have fever and he is of a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauteries are aid for finishing moisters: that is why they are of greater help to the moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	In the extraction of arteries, one should fill the area with old cotton and place good-made drains on top; and when they are undone, you should cure them with dry medicines that cause inflammation, and with drains until it is healed; if without the cutting of the artery as much as you work, you hurry to close it with a cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze your hand so the blood does not coagulate; and if you do not have this, place your hand on the area until it becomes frozen, and apply cold water frequently and squeeze it as needed; and the harder and slower the artery extraction is, the more it will be easier in the cauterization of this cautery with two edges, but they should be well thickened to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the pulse is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives, one of thick distance, and then when you have pierced through both the thicknesses, and you place the fire hot upon it until it reaches the bone, and cut open the vein in two thicknesses; and they shall be separated between the two heads because it is not always sealed by this cautery from all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes flow out of the veins that are above the testicles of the head and there is no benefit to medical treatment made in this case, and you see the patient writhing with pain, and his forehead seems to tremble like in a fit; and if they are thin and moist so that the hair on the scrotum falls out, and the scrotum is burnt and scorched by the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And it shall be called the "contused cure," and you make a cut at the back of the patient who has this disease on his forehead, then you make three cuts evenly along the forehead according to the length of the forehead; and one of the cuts shall be as deep as necessary to reach the jawbone below, and the other two shall be along the cheeks above the eyebrows, and guard yourself from cutting the arteries that are on the cheeks above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the jaws, and each wound shall have the size of three fingers joined together; and prepare a piece of sponge and much of cloth for drying the blood, then push the sharp spatula of two parts into it as shown here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is above the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the cartilage that is between the two cuts completely up to the bone, then proceed from the mid-incision to the other second, and then remove this spatulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the tool called 'cultellaire', which is sharp on one side and soft on the other, not sharp but flexible, and its shape is:
