Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And strike the cutting edge towards the bare flesh, and the striking edge towards the bone, and hit it until it comes to the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head towards the eyes until the incision is continuous to the opening of the bone, and then proceed in the middle incision to the other side; and then press the blood equally, and apply a lining made of old cotton on each incision; and put damp cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar over it, and ensure that no abscesses come in; and on the third day, undo the sutures, and apply a large amount of cold mustard, then the ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a sharp catarrh often comes, and you see the hairs thin and small, blurred vision, burned papers; and the hair follicles are itching, and when the head is scratched in pain, and the sick person coughs; then know by these signs that those materials and that catarrh do not come from any other vein, but rather the one which is affected. The cure for this disease is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you shall instruct the patient to bend their head back, then make a large cut across the forehead, and another in the large bone of the back of the head.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 And begin the cut from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing; and once the bone is exposed, drain all the blood onto a sponge, then apply between the two edges of the cut and place old cotton, and bandage; then cover with damp cloths soaked in vinegar and oil, and be careful not to cause abscess heat; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until char comes to grow, then treat with things that promote growth, which help char grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour, and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster; administer it in these wounds to alleviate pain everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage (clogging) of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ear is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones or similar things such as iron; seeds, peas, beans; or something flowing like water and ashes and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear in any way other than fitting properly or not being aligned with the ear and does not fit inside the ear, place the ear on the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see a stone, apply a little purple oil or camphor oil, then introduce extraction; make him vomit with a concoction, and stop his nostrils when vomiting comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; hold it above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often fumigation comes about with this cure; and if it does not, introduce extraction by subtle tweezers, which is described as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it bursts through the tweezers, that is good; if not, apply extraction using fine and slender scissors; and if it does not burst through this, make a cane of beeswax and push the head of the cane or opening of the ear strongly, and stop what is around the cane with molten wax so that the fumes cannot enter with the cane; then pull it out forcibly, for often times it bursts forth as we have said; and if it does not burst forth in this manner, take glue from wherever you can find it, put it on any device that is sharp for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not burst forth through all the things that we have said, hurry to incise the ear so that abscess comes out and spasms; and the method of incision is that you first anesthetize the patient with opium, then drain the blood according to the strength of its power, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the base of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; and let the incision be as a crescent moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it as far as possible, and suck out hastily to your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is swollen with grain and inflated, administer extraction; and if it cannot be expelled, administer one thin spathule according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 And make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not make that incision if you think the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with subtle forceps and press it with juice, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In water then that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use warm compresses first, and fill the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And lie down on that very ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out because of this, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it does not jump out, take many small and thin pebbles according to the length of your finger and heat them slightly in the fire; then have the patient put one or two fingers into his ear, and press with one stone on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop pressing the stones together until the water completely comes out, and it jumps out completely; and if you see, take a string, and push one of the fingers in the ear, and the other finger grasp fire until the nearest finger is burned; then do another thing with more strings until the water comes out completely, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small animals such as mice and similar things, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large and can be felt, introduce extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earwigs, when you treat it as we have said in the previous section or using distillations which do not help, if there are no worms visible, take fine tweezers and grasp them at this shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And it should be narrow beneath and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And the thin tip should be inserted into the ear according to the intensity of the patient's pain, then proceed to suck out entirely the canine; do this often until all the worm emerges.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 If they do not come out, stop the canine with cotton as I said in the previous section; if they do not protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective for treating worms, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this device as shown here:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is to be made of silver or lead which is inserted into small openings, and on top with a distilling dish; and for pressing inside the distillation, use one instrument of lead well made for this purpose. And if you see a plug and wrap it around the point with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see fit in the pipe, and let the pipe be in the ear. Then push the plug into the cotton and press gently until the oil distills or becomes hot in the ear. Let the patient smell inside, and the distillation should be heated with fire so it is as it is distilled in the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be good if it is too cold.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage (clogging) of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without having some opening in the ears; and this same thing happens with adults due to ear injury or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage sometimes occurs deep within the ear, if one cannot see it; and sometimes there is a small hole in the ear, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it comes out completely and cannot be seen, it is serious healing in many positions, and in such a case, you must put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening clearly apparent, then open it with this spatula of the form specified here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And sharp and cutting in front and behind entirely, so as not to burn the ear; if the opening is of cartilage or skin of the ear, hold it with subtle tweezers, and gently remove it all.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the inflammation is deep in the ear, take a sharp, delicate tweezers and heat them slightly over fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the inflammation that causes the patient to feel pain in the ear, pierce it lightly, ensuring not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert a wick according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound heals: take a cloth and soak it in strong rosewater, and powder vitriol over it (broken); if you see the ear swelling, then pull out the cloth and apply another cloth soaked in salve made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling disappears; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If discharge of blood comes out, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments to remove the blood discharge which are called distillations.
de la char des papieres	of paper charcoal (carbon)
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that come in paper from the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tweezers and forceps, and strike it with a spatula from its roots; then put on the place vitriol ground.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	If not removed by other means, then cauterize the lenticular cautery gently and slowly, and cauterize after the incision is beneficial; and many times they heal again, for nothing stays from their roots; and when cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and will not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often come in paper the eyes are found some things resembling hail in shape and hardness, and because of this is this disease called "grandine", and it is a large amount of moisture in the paper above and below; the work is such: take care that the grandine does not move from both sides, and this is easy to know; then make an incision on the widest part, then peel each side lightly, then take with tweezers and squeeze.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it with a bandage without piercing through a little paper, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the wound is large, join it together with a stitch, and let it heal until it is healed; and if it is small, do not put too much force on it, because the salve will heal it quickly and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the grandine is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and take hold of the grandine with forceps, squeeze and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is pushed away by the incision, then do not cause pain; when the grandine is squeezed, apply salted oil to the wound and care for the affected area until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 This is a salve that is applied on papers for children more than adults, and it causes much harm to their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears flow quickly to their eyes; and therefore, they lie down immediately on their faces, sleep, and keep their papers wet under their eyelids, which keeps the salve from opening in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the dislocation inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head on a clean surface; then take one linen cloth and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach from each part, and place it above; then press between your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make an incision in the middle with a sharp spatula, and not larger than the wound made in vein suture; and cut through the skin as far as you see the exinach; and in various positions, exinach comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then hold the piece of coarse cloth between your hands and turn your hand to the left and right until it is dispersed; and be careful not to widen the incision or reach the oil with the spatula, do not cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the beginning of the cut, lift up the wound slightly; then pull it apart as we have said, wet some bandages with oil and water, place them on the wound, and hold it in place with bindles.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if such men who grind and place it on top to corrupt the moisture that remains there.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure it until it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the joint becomes an abscess that is hot, then cure it with plasters soothing until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like hairs grow on the eyelids that are not natural and they are nurtured, they harm the eyes and bring about types of diseases such as constant tearing and softening of the paper-like growths, which causes destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to cure them: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicine for ague according to what was mentioned in the previous chapter on cauterization, or by incision and suturing, or by caustics, as I shall explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head on your healthy side, then turn the paper-like growth from the eye towards your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, push an awl with one filament through it; and remove the margin of the paper or the hair that grows from those hairs, taking one filament across the entire paper, and shave it off; then make a shallow groove in the part beneath the paper, below the hairs, covering the entire spatula blade from the large tear to the small; then pull out one filament, and place a small tent made of cotton and linen under the paper, then mark on the paper a figure of an anchor, like the seed of mirte, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the size that you see raising the paper which has been previously determined.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if there is someone who needs a large amount of paper according to how soft the paper is; then they must put it all on top of the wound for three lines that you have marked, and start from the larger blister up to the smaller; and one of the cuts should be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the onion in one of the two angles of the wound, then remove the husk; then bring the two sides together with a stitch using a fine needle and linen thread, squeeze the blood, and tie the excess threads to anything sticky, if you want to do this; but if not, do not cure it, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days; then heal the wound without the stitch with drying and constricting things, because the paper sticks to the edge of the wound and the assembly, but the stitch is rotten (as they say in ancient times), and this is a laborious process without fear; and there is another way: it is that you sign the paper in the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have counted, with three onions cut according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then make that which surmounts the small points equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you are unable to hold the tongs, and the thing is not even, take a needle with thread, and insert it through the figure; insert the larger thread from the large incision, and the smaller thread from the small, and arrange the threads equally between your hands; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin as you have described, then stitch up the edges of the wound using a suture, and heal it until it is healthy; if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar calming substances; and sometimes the hair of the paper turns: in this case, use what we have said about the incision; however, stitching on one side or the other is more difficult.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of cancers is as follows: you should convert the paper and place it inside according to what I have said, then make two cages by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and width as broad as the spatula is; and bind the two pieces together where the threads are; then assemble the one and the other carefully on top of the paper with oil, and bind the two cages from the two parts; leave it for some days, and the skin that has been bound will die, rot, and fall off, leaving a hole.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it takes a long time, if he hits it with force, then heal him until he is healthy; and when the wound has been stitched up, and the paper has risen, and the hair will not grow anymore; this is the shape of the two canines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The first sentence to translate:
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the channel (tunnel) is treated and the hairs do not come out, then draw the channel down to the length of the thread you have arranged, until the channel comes out from the opening above and you see it through the oil; then draw out the channel and the thread, close the eye and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair adheres in its place and grows new skin over it; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long natural hair and let it grow with it, until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the abscess (boil) of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease which is called "alecraty" or the boils come in the eye, there are two ways it may happen: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 It happens by sudden wounding, cutting or burning, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 The method of work in this case is that you split the wound, separate the lips from it, put cotton of flax inside, and hold it until it heals; and it is not advisable to use anything in its cure that dries or constricts.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 If you do this, the disease worsens more than the first; but in the work of softening things, such as fenugreek; and the juice of water or vinegar cooked with flax seeds should be heated until it thickens into any oil, and then wrap it in a linen cloth and apply it to that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the remedy for your cure is to ensure that it does not heal in the same way as before; and this work that we have said is not effective unless proper attention is paid to this disease, so that it does not return in its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the fat that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease which is truly called "axacrati", and is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things; and the work process in it is that you take a needle with a double thread, and pierce the skin on the left eyelid until it reaches the other, so that the threads come out in the two cheeks of the skin; then stretch the skin above the whole needle, and rub with a large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shoulder figure of the paper returns as it should, it is good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the crack, and turn the paper, and make two cracks where the bone protrudes inside the paper; and let the heads of the two cracks be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and let an angle be formed so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter with the name "Greek"; then remove that cartilage, according to the amount that its sides are sharpened beneath the paper, then join the two separated parts with a linen thread; then treat it as we have said for medicines softening and for drawing pus, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the sickness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, then you must make a deep incision under the hairs of the paper, as described earlier; then you should draw out between the two layers of the skin like I said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters prepare devices with all their might to return the figure to its natural form; and the sick themselves, according to what work and instruments are required in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the hairs of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sewing occurs in the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is sewn with white oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural work, then you must insert the tip of a razor blade under the paper, lift it up; and stretch it using pliers until you reach the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too pointed, so that the sick man does not suffer from the too-sharp spatula causing damage to the oil; and your incision, from which you peel off the assembled area, should be gentle, allowing the paper to return to its natural form; and heal all of the assembled area, making it sometimes in oil of vinegar unsalted and sweet leaven, then put a tent made of linen between the paper and oil, and place wool dampened with egg on top of the oil; and after three days use warm water and healing salves until it heals.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the finger
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail has two kinds: it is either nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, or it's not nerve-like but resembles white congealed moisture that, when touched by iron and cooked with tweezers, cannot be removed; and both begin at the great cuticle and grow little by little until they cover the whole nail and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take a piece of paper with your hand, then take the nail with tweezers of small double curvature and hold it above; then take a needle and put one horse hair or ox hair and a strong thread on it; bend the tip of the needle slightly and pierce through the nail, and pass the whole needle through it, tie the nail with a thread and hold it above, and peel off all the skin from the side of the nail that was close to the cuticle and the silk until the hair reaches the head, then chop off the remaining in the root of the cuticle with every subtle spatula and small force, and leave the natural skin or cuticle so that no blood comes out of the cuticles as usual; and sometimes the nail is incised only on the edge and at the tip, as we have said; then peel off all the spatumile from it in this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the spatula does not touch the skin layer and break it, and that the prunelle is not pierced; and after incision pour oil a small amount of boiled egg yolk and let it rest with a litargire collar, leave it until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous and you cannot insert the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, this condition of the nail is often treated with medicines; and they grow as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, then open the oil of the patient, take the spatula gently and slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Lift the nail gently and if you see that it does not shrink and the reason is pressing on it, then distill from your mouth collyrium made of litargyre and red collyrium and boiled egg yolk into the oil and stopper it until the next day; then continue the other work according to this same procedure until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing contradicts you in oil (i.e., if it is an abscess), then let it discharge, and first heal the abscess with hot water until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the arm is harmful in oil (meaning an abscess) by great damage, then suspend it at the joint and cut off a part but not too much, so that tears do not come; then distill red colloidal oil made of litargyre (an antimony compound).
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which arises on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 For some men, a red char [pusule] sometimes arises, which covers the nail and lies on top of the paper and turns it backwards, resembling a rose bud; and the treatment for this is that the patient holds his head in your hand, then you operate on the nails, and whatever char [pusule] arises should be removed with suitable instruments and held firmly; then cut the first char, and proceed cutting until smooth to the root, ensuring not to puncture the oil at the operation; and the incision should be made with a spatula as described in the treatment of the nail and small instruments like those used for excising a splinter, according to the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the char [pusule] removed, apply oil of sulphur ground or you distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and place defuer cotton with egg white on top, so that it is secure against infection; and if anything remains, and the wound becomes inflamed, and you doubt that it is infected, leave the oil and treat the inflammation with cooling agents for reducing inflammation; then return to your operation until it heals, and do as described above for all char [pusules] treated in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must lighten the cure of each oil with natural methods; and in case of accidental injury, in work involving iron; and never insert your hand into any of these operations unless you see that the limb is strong enough to endure that operation.
des voines des eulz	The veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 When veins become red that are covered with oil and they do not show their work and weaken the oil for all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Firstly, it is necessary to examine if the problem with the oil (sebel) exists and there is no other disease. Then you must proceed as follows: instruct the patient to lean his head on your hand, then hold the veins firm for the entire duration according to your wisdom, and make the ties twice as thin as shown in this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two lengths of the cloth folded twice by degree, as follows:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then collect the veins subtly with force, and squeeze out the blood hour after hour, until you see the veins move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatula, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that only these veins are affected; and when you have done this, if it distills into green and red coloured oil for correcting what is left behind in the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and sure of abscessing coldly, then resume according to this manner as long as it is healthy; and this is the form of force:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, there is a cavity in it where it should die, and you must cut open the abscess along that area, removing all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, then use all the equipment that is shown here; it is called "rough head", and should be made of iron and shaped like this (referring to a certain shape as presented in the drawing):
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the bone that is corrupted, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is crushed; do this repeatedly, then restore the position of the medicine extractors.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the joint is fused, and char (pus) arises, and the body of the bone is fused, and it remains in this state for forty days, and it does not heal or become abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, knowing that it is healthy; if not, there is no other remedy but to return the fistula (abscess) to the opening of the neck according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone for a second time with iron, and with medicines made hot, and when it is uncovered, take the probe according to this form, and let the tip of the iron be at three angles, and let the rod be tapered towards the top as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place the probe on the bone in the notch, and move your hand away from the wound hole, then turn the probe around until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through this because the pus is flowing out if he holds his hand on the neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the pus hardens the joint, the matter goes to the neck; it will be easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the nasal passage
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no disturbance to the ship [the body], and it does not decrease, you must hold the patient; then clean [the eyes], then apply plasters or ointment without causing pain, then apply oil - a liniment made from aloe, acacia, incense, and saracocolla - and hold [the eye], and apply the plaster on bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then place one on top of another according to the amount required by the eyes; then hold it together with a tough bandage and repeat the application of plasters without causing pain; then remove the plasters and leave the oil held for day and night, and if the liniment becomes soft, you must hold it firmly; then remove the liniment after day and night, and if you see the eyes heal, that is good; if not, repeat the application of the plaster and the liniment and the bandages until the eyes are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The bursting of a swollen cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the uvea (the middle layer of the eye), followed by an opening and forced expulsion of paper-like substances resembling grain of resin and appearing alarming; then if you see it covered, the treatment is such that you insert a needle into the root of the affected area up to where it is above, then insert another needle with double thread from the edge of the wound; and make it pierce through, leaving the first needle according to its position; then hold the eye's lid tightly and tie a part of the uvea around it, applying pressure; then remove the needle and apply oiled linen cloth abundantly over the area; and leave it until the threads stick with the uvea, then cure the affected area with soothing substances until the wound heals; and at times, the wound is restrained by the uvea on each side of a circular bandage of fabric, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes seem large in appearance, perforate them with a thin spatula filled with oil, remove the albuginea (the middle layer of the eye) and drain the fluid from the eyes; then let it heal completely.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the beak of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from being an abscess assembled in the oil, resembling an inflamed watery swelling, and it is not inflamed; and the appearance of its work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the abscess rise above your eyes; then it should be lanced, and the swelling should not decrease and the light should be cleared, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not decrease below, know that it is inflamed, and if the removal of the abscess is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Make the patient sit between your hands, then take the thin spatula and press it against the corneal membrane at the conjunctiva with the cornea and the bone, as long as the bubble forms; when it is out, distill into it sharp hot oil mixed with honey or hot oil and fenugreek boiled with honey, then treat it with another cure until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	oil abscesses
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have similar symptoms to the eyes in the division, and what is needed to pierce it; if you follow accordingly according to its health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit crossed between your hands, away from sunlight, and hold the oil clean and tight very strongly; then put the paper of the oil in your left hand if the eye is on the left side or in your right hand if the eye is on the right side; then take in your right hand (if the eye is on the left side) the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand (if the eye is on the right side); then put the tip of the instrument against the cornea along the thickness of a nail in that white part of the oil at the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and hold your hand as long as it pierces through the white part of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty place; and it is necessary that the measurement of the way almagda be at the full measure of the space which is from the eyelid to the end of the iris; and this is the cornea of the oil; then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then put the instrument until it reaches the place where the water is, then press it down along another way.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If the knife is drawn now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in its oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a short pause, and if the knife moves up again along the second vein, push the force with the instrument, and when it is fully inserted and does not move any further, lightly twist your hand back and forth; then apply another little gemstone oil to it from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then apply the oil of poppy or linen moistened in rose oil and egg oil, and bind with oil from a healthy person.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those who are of our time, put on it a dressing made of much egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the gemstone oil cannot enter due to hardness, because some men have very hard eyes, then you must take the tool called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 Therefore, only perforate the conjunctive, and do not go too deeply, but make it subtle, then put in much oil, as we have said; and when the work is complete, arrange the patient to sleep on his back in a dark place; he should be free of all movements, eat light foods, move neither right nor left, and bind him according to his position until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark place, examine his vision, show him some things, and then re-bind him for seven days; it is not necessary that you do this during the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you let it heal because the knife rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess has come to a head, you should open the oil before the seventh day, and follow the instructions of those who soothe an abscess; and when it is soothed, you should then lance the eye (of the abscess) and place golden ointment over it to cover for any number of days, and remain always in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 Then leave the house little by little, and turn to his own affairs; and know that no disciple should meddle with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iram, who told us that in their country everyone has a large pear-shaped swelling, so that fluid accumulates, but I have never seen anyone with such a thing in our land, nor have I read of it in the books of ancient people; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of almagda shapes, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of linen properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these (should) be in the same subtlety, and the rear ones in four corners.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes there are born or grow various cysts, of which some appear like scorpions with many heads; and if there are such or if the cyst is inflamed in a yellowish color, and if it swells with a white color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In such cases of soft cartilage that is not hardened, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, pour the onion juice into those cartilages, and pull them out; then grasp what you can sustain with a fine, sharp spatula from one side, until you know that that cartilage is entirely detached.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be covered, you shall open it all, i.e., with subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if there is no pus, or an abscess covered, help it as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the pus is drained and all the charred matter is removed, then pour in oil, vinegar, or hot water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nostrils are not opened and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is healthy; if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is a cartilage growing in the bone above, which the instrument does not come to cut: then you must tie a thick piece of flax, moisten it with your hands, and leave space between each knot as necessary; place the patient's chin in the flax with all his might, pulling it out through the nose while smelling; and children in school often do this many times, and it is easy for whoever wants to do it; then hold one head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know each other while we who are holding the flax.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Make sure you know that the nose has been corrupted by corruption of the flesh, then pull out the thread, squeeze the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian oil and put it back to its place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then put a plank splint on the nose for any number of days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as oil and medicines are distilled near the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or brass, resembling a lamp with a closed neck, and you shall lead it so; and if you see, make a closed tube, and the instruments should be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often in the head of the nose there arises a sickness called "telul", which grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye; and for this reason you must cut it at the beginning, and burn it completely with cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed too long while it is still small, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an aggravated abscess, for when one touches it in any way, much harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of a dark color, and you can cover it completely, let the patient empty it and cut it cautiously without fear, and cure the place with dry things that absorb.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution of synovial fluid comes into one of these articular cavities, it does not help much, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when this happens to anyone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; then press the two lips together with a stitch, heal it until it is healed; and if the edges are separated from one side and the other, you must scrape all the parts of their edge until they heal, then press the two lips together with a stitch and tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood, and incense powder on top; and place a piece of plaster of strong or another plaster adhering to it, and let it remain until it dries, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as I have told you in the belly stitch; or with thread, as we mentioned earlier.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses from lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	For men, within the lips there occurs an abscess hard, similar to grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut open each one, take it with tweezers and crush it in every part; afterwards apply the vitriol powder to the wound until the blood is stopped; then apply alum to heal the wound until it heals completely.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often arises on the gums a swelling called "albulus"; you should hold it with tweezers and crush it at its root, allowing the pus to flow out; then apply powdered vitriol or other drying and constricting powders to the area; if the swelling returns after cutting, which often happens, you should crush it again and cauterize it; it does not return after cauterization; these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	The sores
