Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, sores are assembled in the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scabs that are unsightly; and sometimes the tooth becomes black and yellow and hollow as corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth stinks; you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and scrape the teeth or scabs that appear, until nothing remains; and do the same for the blackness and greenness, and for the yellowish and other blemishes, until they are cleaned; and if you remove that which is at the root first, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, as long as you have everything removed; and know that teeth require different forms of instruments to scrape them, according to what the work requires, because the scraper used to clean the teeth has other shapes than the one used between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a tooth for pain, you must delay extraction as much as possible, because it should not be done at all; for it is a very high substance up until the point that there is no excuse to shave.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is compelled to draw (a tooth), you must be sure about the tooth to be drawn.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the patient suffers from pain that he thinks is a toothache, and pulls out the good tooth; but the pain does not cease until the bad one comes out, as we have often seen in such cases; and when you are certain of the tooth to be pulled, it is necessary that you isolate the tooth with strong forceps all around. Then move it towards your fingers or subtle pliers at the first root and root, until it is completely dislocated, then firmly hold the pliers; and keep the patient's head between your knees, and hold him so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After straightening the tooth properly to break it, if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and gently push it from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten through, it must be filled with cloths, where the holes are; and if you squeeze it gently with pliers so as not to break while squeezing; and it must be very carefully operated around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it and leave a part remaining, as the patient will suffer even greater pain due to the malice of the root afterwards.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act like the ignorant lords who in haste and rashness sometimes break a cart, yet they never bring what we have mentioned; but they often cause great disease by the roots that remain or by the cart they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the place with wine or vinegar and oil; and if bleeding comes, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, which quiet the tooth roots first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron, and toothed to hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains in pulling, it is necessary that you put soft cotton soaked in butter on its place for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the joints are softened, then insert the tweezers called "algefri", so that the head resembles a spur of a thorn; and inside make them like a clamp and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all those tools, you must peel back the skin all around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as a pincer, of which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Be large and thick so as not to break it, and if the root jumps out through these tools, that is good; otherwise, use all the instruments, of which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one assists with this instrument having two prongs, of which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and of this tool which appears to be large pliers, in its form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool should not break, and know that many instruments for teeth are; and also other tools which are not counted; and the wise masters discover their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the disease shows, because there are such diseases where the old did not teach any tool due to diversity in each case; and if it breaks the cart or another bone where it should be, then look for the tools that are required, which I told you, and help with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone, but not slip away, but be able to hold and remove it; then restore the place of medicines suitable for that, and if there is pus in the bone and it is small, use all this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape, and the form is ugly, even in women virgins, you must know if the tooth is not born after the dent, and it is not in the correct place, and cannot be corrected or smoothed: then file [the tooth]; and if it is exposed with the tooth, take this instrument, as shown by the form below, resembling a small beak, made of sharp iron at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle of the file is held in hands for long hours due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be smoothed, file it with a flat file as shown below:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is similar to the file used for making needles; and file the tooth little by little with the file in hands gently, so it does not move too much while chewing; then plane the end entirely with any file, and if the root is too sharp and it bites the tongue, you must smooth the sharpness until it is even, so it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth are loose or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on it without it chattering, and you have cured them with constricting medicines, but this does not work; then you must bind it with a gold thread, as silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and the thread should be medium-sized neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you direct the teeth, take the thread and place it double between the two loose teeth, then put the head between the molars if there is one or more, as long as you see clearly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the covering up to the part where you started, and hold your hand skillfully and carefully, so that it does not move; and tie your knot at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then thread the shoulders with a wire using pliers, and assemble them, and place them so that they do not pierce the tongue; and then leave them as tight as they can remain, and if they dislocate or break, tie another wire; if it remains and serves thus throughout its duration, this is the shape of teeth and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth and two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place, as we have said; and let no one who is not skilled and patient interfere with it; and sometimes the shape of a bone tooth from an animal is made and placed at the place where it lacks, and it should be held and served for a long time as described earlier.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes this ligament comes beneath the tongue by nature or due to an accidental wound; and the operations are such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head steady, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve ligament widely until the ligament is dislocated from its position, and if there is hardness or knotting, this is a sudden wound, in which case you apply an unguent and cut widely that ligament; and be careful not to make the incision too deep, for the artery that is beneath; and when you have done this, lift the level of rosewater or warm water, then place under the tongue a linen tent; and press the patient each night so that the level does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding occurs, put on it vitriol powder; and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with slow-burning cautery (which is good for this); then heal it with another treatment until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of dark or black color or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards blistering, and there is moisture, throw in an arrowhead, and make a small incision on both sides with a thin spatula, and free it from one side and the other; and if the blood does not stop at your work, apply vitriol powder until it is drained completely; then raise the rose-colored and ashen level, and cure it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	The abscess of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes boils called "godath" come up inside the throat, and they are correctly called the two almonds; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they do not heal, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will cut it open, or it would burst by itself; and if it is of white color again, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument for covering, but first make sure that the abscess is calm and soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders should be in a straight position, and he opens his mouth and the servant takes him between his hands, pressing the tongue beneath all the instrument, as shown here; and it should be made of silver or thin iron, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue under the entire instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the awl and poke it into the almond, and pull it upwards as much as you can; pull any fabric away from there, then cover it with the instrument, so that this is its shape, like a vise; and although the head may be bent, one end to another, and they are very sharp, made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the coppersmith's pliers, of which form is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the coppersmith's pliers, of which form is as follows: grasp one of the almonds and squeeze the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot, sharp, and astringent substance, and if bleeding occurs, gargarize the patient with hot, or scorches of green grapes cooked, or twigs of myrtle, and similar things until the wound is cauterized; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses than the two almonds may appear in the throat, if they appear, squeeze them in the same way as the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 Then treat a woman with an abscess inside the throat, that is of small size; and had tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked passageway, nor eat or drink, and would have died within a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 The abscess had risen so much that it was raised two fingers through the two openings of the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I immediately did so, and drove a splint into one side, then twisted it violently, and drove out a large portion of pus; afterwards, I reset the other shoulder wound and opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; next, I drove the splint into those abscesses and took some part of it out, but only a little blood came out; and thus I removed the woman's throat, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess continued to grow and fill the cavity I had made until it became quite large; so I tied it up and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the anus protrudes towards the outside and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and rounded, it is called "anus".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit at all, and you see that the abscesses are subsiding, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is rounded and not long, and it is red, bloody or black, then you should make an incision for it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it as I have said according to its bladder and length, you should make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the probe into the anus and draw it out, and cut it in two at the places where I said to make an incision in the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cover the superfluous part which is beyond the natural limit, for if you do, it grieves the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what has been said in the incision of the two hands, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient fears to cover [it], then you must use an instrument for the cauterization of the senses to remove fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery is sharp heat.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient places his head in your hand, and then you press his tongue to the instrument that we have said or in the chapter of cauterization, and hold it with sharp live heat, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the tip of this instrument, as shown by its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a comb or hand put the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine without going down to the throat, and the blood. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, the amount of half an hour, until you see it swell and the bites of the medicine are alleviated; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument to the entire cotton into the canal above, until the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this repeatedly, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for 4 or 5 days. And if you need to start the cautery of the medicine again, restart it, and after the cautery suck out around the eye, with a cotton swab in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and wash it with cold water, and treat it with gargarisms until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not just cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camomile and yarrow and origanum and rue and wormwood and similar herbs, put them all together or any of these in one pot, and place it on the fire; let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have one instrument with hair according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the cheeks pushed into the patient's mouth until the steam rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is mortified; afterwards, it often starts again, until the eye dries up, and ensure that you do not perform this at the beginning of an abscess's emergence, for many things happen therein; and do not do this except when in the decline of an abscess's heat.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell fragment in the patient's mouth so that it does not become too hot; for the eggshell fragment does not burden the mouth with steam, and it is good treatment along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it [the abscess] adheres to the throat with bone or splinter of fish, or something else; therefore, you must pull what you can see, and press the tongue against the instrument until you see movement in it; and if that does not open up and returns to the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will expel the thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of seaweed, or a radish root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie one thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, if it adheres, you must pull on the thread; and if it does not come out as we have said, take one stick according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and raise the head high; and watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, as both will come to harm, nor push the bone in; instead, it is better for the patient to push the instrument, because he may be moved or the thing is loose; if he pushes down, or draws it back completely, keep pushing equally until it has gone.
de la sansue de la gorge	the saliva from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the saliva is a medicine, as I said in the division, by treating with medicines; and when it does not benefit at all, then look at the patient's throat towards the sun, and when you press his tongue on the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the saliva, draw it out with a very small spoon or subtle tweezers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that does not work, take a heated iron rod and insert it into the patient's throat, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And make the patient drink water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth and pour it in so that he may swallow it, and move his head with your hand often; and as soon as the saliva feels the water, he will spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, you should fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the uve fumigation; do this many times, for it will persistently weep.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The manner of fumigation is as follows: Take a pot with charcoal in it, and cover it with a perforated cloth in the middle, and place the head of the instrument inside; then pour your fumigation into it. Have the patient hold the head of the cane in his mouth, close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes directly to the wound; at this point, the wound should weep, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times; have the patient endure thirst, eat only salty and acidic foods, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to pass through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument to treat the nose, is like corbeled tweezers for entering the throat; and resembling the beak of a syringe, and having asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot lose; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	Chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many things similar to an abscess are mentioned below in this chapter, according to what memory comes later from one and another in this book; they are different in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways that one is like itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for the joints that are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 because abscesses of the head are different than those in the body, and abscesses of the charnut bone are different than those that come in joints, and each should be judged according to its work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses, one should not pierce them unless the bowel is mature according to its completion; and if there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are hardened, but do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that come from joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 Because an abscess comes from the disruption of joints, and it is left until it bursts around, possibly corrupting the ligament and nerve in the joint; this is why there is contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 For the abscess is to be lanced from the main member, and if you delay the perforation until it has ripened, it will harm the main member; or it is lanced from the base, if it is pierced before it has died; and it must not be lanced without proper digestion, except that which is lanced from the base, which cannot penetrate entirely and become long inside, and a fistula forms and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you must know the time of perforation of the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the disappearance of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and reduction in size of the abscess head, and other signs; and you should make a small incision in the perforation area that depends on the location of the abscess, and where it has opened; and the perforation should be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and in all even places where there is no pus."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that drop, according to the same limb. (direct translation of the given Old French sentence)
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a charred place, it's good to leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce before it, the body will follow the flow of the fluid and fill with much filth; and inadvertently, it hardens the lips and deepens the wound from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to the needs of the limbs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 It's necessary that you make small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is required to cauterize, cover; when it has become as a piece of cloth, and softened, it's necessary to do it as with infants: and if it has been cut into three angles, and if there are those from which you cauterize like the twigs of myrtle, abscesses from the joints; and if it is such that a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar shapes, to be cauterized.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 He who has no head (like an abscess superficially), it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large, and it contains a big bowel, and you pierce it, do not draw out the whole bowel in that hour, but draw out a part; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing wrongly; do this repeatedly with great care until the bowel goes out entirely.  Similarly, if the patient is weak, or a woman, or small children, or old people decrepit, perform this with great care.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The sphincter sometimes twitches with the passage of the bowel, which may accidentally cause the death of the patient, and you must not worry about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, be careful with this chapter, and when you have pierced the abscess, if the wound is small, apply a piece of linen or old cotton to it; and if it is a large abscess and there is much pus, you must insert a piece of linen or new linen cloth in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin and shaved it around, fill it with old cotton or woolen cloth without moisture, and bind it for up to three days; then open it and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, apply cold water and linen cloth, moisten it, and place on the site repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If bleeding persists in your work, apply a treatment and remedy, and the powders I have mentioned in this book to the affected areas, and if it is winter, or the wounds or abscesses are very nerve-racking, you should place hot cloths and linen drenched in oil and wine on top of them; but if it's summer and the wound is fleshy, you should put cold cloths drenched in water and oil or cool oil on it for three days, then drain and treat the abscess, as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: here I have told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and now comes the chapter.
des soros	on les faut oster et conforter par l'aiguille et les poudres
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses on the head, it is our practice that they are covered with linen, similar to how a grape is wrapped, and there are many similarities in this regard.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fat and others that have moisture like pulses; there are also those that are hard and stony at the base, but there is no doubt that the arteries do not oppose them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the procedures of the waist are that you test everything called "entromissoire", from which the shape comes next, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they make a long incision through it.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is drained, they scrape the skin that contains it without leaving any hair, for it quickly returns if left; then place cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise in vinegar and linen, and apply it to the wound and leave until the next day; those who remain will heal.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the lint, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know that it does not stay clean; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 If the abscess remains full of pus, press it in this manner, longwise; and pour out your onions and peel off all the skin, and put all your care into drawing pus from the cavity where it lies; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I have said before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise treat the abscess if it is pustular, and cut and care for it as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 Cut above the pustular abscess and moisten it, if possible, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if any of these abscesses or head has no moisture, and among those was the abscess which I cut from an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard as a quartz stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had struck it with iron, it would have caused the same injury as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses or heads coming from children and roots of ears, open them always at the earliest depending on location, in order to promote drainage; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of the scrofula (scrofulas)
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times this abscess occurs at the neck, under the chin, and in the armpits, and sometimes it occurs elsewhere on the body, and they are large, and join together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 Each scrofula is properly within its side, just like the swelling and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities in these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 Some of them contain moisture, and some are malevolent and refuse to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In the one that you see with good disposition on the toucher (palpation), and is similar in color to the body, and silent from every part and not pressed against the neck or artery or conduit, and not pulsating; then you must cut it open from above, and peel off each portion, and apply the two lips of the incision to the incision in the swelling of the head as we have said, and draw it out gently and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and it should not be sharp, lest the hand slips, and it does not see too far ahead, so that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you open the vein or the artery and it does not let you pass, put vitriol powder or some powders that stop blood in the wound, hold the wound closed; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound becomes soft and starts to break open.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 When the blood has stopped, return to your work, until you finish it; then ask your assistant if there remain any small scrophulas, if so, cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a vein scrophula with a large root, it is not necessary to cut that scrophula at its root, but tie it up with a strong double thread and let it hang down without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cover the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now as there will be no excess remaining due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas that have excess, perforate there where it is more open; and perforate as the one before said, depending on it, then bring in tents with ointment and similar things so that they corrupt what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment made from bright charcoal until it is healed.
de squinance	And if you excise the entire squinchy bump (a term used to describe a lump or swelling in medieval medicine), it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them up immediately since there will be no excess due to the size of the squinchy bump. It is necessary that you understand to cover the root and draw pus out, and sew as we have said before. Those squinchy bumps with superfluidity (excessive fluid), pierce where it has grown closed; and pierce as described above, depending on it, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply a charmed ointment until it heals.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the shape of the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinch (a condition), the slit in the throat called "epiglottis" should be opened; and no help should be given by those with abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in 2 tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the throat, it should be covered to prevent the danger of choking caused by strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut through 3 or 4 small circles or a narrow slit between two of them, and not in the cartilage; and those parts should be suitable for cutting the epiglottis so that there is no cartilage, and the veins are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to its entire length, then cuts the neck until it reaches the Adam's apple; and avoid the veins of blood, if you see any, and then cut the trachea, as we have said; and it has been demonstrated by the section of the jugular vein that flows through the broken joint and the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, bring the two lips of the wound together gently, and close it completely with a splint; then administer medicines that promote healing, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi said not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient has been judged dead and the breath has left him/her.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then press on the windpipe because the patient cannot cough, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, which passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it when cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 A young girl took the knife, stabbed herself in the throat, and injured her windpipe; I was called to treat her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw the blood coming out of it, and knew that it had not opened up or been directed anywhere other than the throat, and the wind was going through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was well again; the girl did not suffer from speech loss, but returned to her normal state; for this reason, do not fear in similar situations of the windpipe.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in color like a pustule, and it is very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; where natural has no device.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 The accidental one is also of two kinds, where one resembles swollen glands, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from the artery; there should be caution, and it should not be operated on except in the case of a small one, and it must be probed and examined thoroughly: if you find it similar to swollen glands, and it does not open at all, if you squeeze it, as you would with glands, and pull it off completely, if there is any; and surround it well, and cure it as necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of ours are [described], and I will say all their similarities; now it is necessary that I tell the entire difference between knot and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue (discharge) is heat and fever lasting, until the eruptions have passed, and the purification has been completed; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With knot there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the knot itself, which is its own sac and is similar to the color of the body, and begins in the same way as a boil, and grows larger; and they are of two types, fat or moist, and their color is much like what I said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the care of the sick, that you test and inquire first about all the equipment which is called "entromissoire", according to its form or the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 The method of treating abscesses in the body is to take the moistest place that you find within the abscess and gradually rotate your fingers, until you feel that the straw has pierced the core; this will depend on the size of the abscess; then extract the contents, but be careful not to let any escape.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs out from the abscess, let it be drained as I have said for other abscesses; and if after opening there comes no more moisture, know that it is full, then make a cross-shaped incision, take hold of it with forceps, and gently scrape it lightly from both sides and pull out the cavity where it lies, ensuring you draw it out healthy with the thread; and if you cannot draw it out healthily, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If nothing remains, it will return multiple times; and if a small amount remains, which does not distress you, apply some corrosive powder to the wound, bind the wound, place something soothing on the abscess warmly, and treat it with other remedies until it heals; and if it is large, make two incisions at the edge of the wound, and treat it with what makes the flesh heal.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein bursts against you or another, hurry and use vitriol powder, let it lie for two or four days, until the wound scabs over, and let the pus of blood settle; then cover what remains of the wound with a poultice.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of the instruments for incision, and they come in three ways: large, medium, and small; and among them there are three cross shapes called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are also three sizes: large, medium, and small, used to encircle abscesses with fistula; and they are similar to needles used for sewing charms, and made of bronze, iron, or silver, and the yellow ones work better, and the black ones are more experienced in closing fistula furrows; and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the incisions are similar to one another as you can see: large, medium, and small; and some have two curved parts, also in three ways; some have three curved parts, and these are also in three ways; some have two curved parts, and some with only one curved part, and these are also in three ways; and all of this is necessary for their purpose.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The first part of the shoulder that is cut open are sharp, and those who do not cut completely from one side, with this method we scrape the nerves, as it is not good to damage the vein; and these intrusive bones are replaced in multiple ways, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one should not use this method but in the charnut region (the upper arm), such as the legs, arms, breasts, and genitals, and sometimes another small instrument is used, resembling fistula scrapers, according to this form, for draining blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at the location that bleeds to stop the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes again according to this large form:   (This translation assumes that "copement des voines" refers to stopping the bleeding of the veins, which might not be accurate without more context.)
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like those of a woman; and they remain ugly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them must do so according to this form as described in this line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then scrape the fat, and apply the wound with a healing ointment, then bring together the two lips of the wound to stitch, and heal it until it is healed; and if the breast inclines downwards and is deformed due to its size as happens in women, divide it into two halves above, by two similar cuts; thus one will be holding onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from line b to line g; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, remove the fat, and introduce what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it digests the remaining fat, then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses from the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses coming from the buttocks are types of scrofulas (hard) or they may contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bowel in the abscess is emptied, you should use old cotton for the wound and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and heal it with an ointment until it becomes healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula (or scrofulous lesions), then make incisions in it as we have said before for scrofula, and if the wound becomes swollen, bring fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The cutting of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is stretched and the skin above it is connected, there are often abscesses, and this also happens at an inflamed vein and abscess; and if one recognizes it by the artery, the abscess is long in depth; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels strangely tight; and when it is due to the vein, it appears round and swollen; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, and especially when it is near the bones and angles, and very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary to remove the iron cure and also the one at the head should be removed; and in the one who is swollen with an artery, make an incision above the skin lengthwise; then open the abdomen carefully, separate the artery from the fat, until it is exposed; then insert a needle and pierce it to the other side of the body, and tie the artery with a double thread as I have instructed in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then press the area between the two bands with an intruder until the swelling subsides which is there, and release the abscess; then apply the cure that binds the bow, until the ligament cries out; then treat it with ointment appropriate to it, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to the vein opening, you must stain your hand with the discharge from the abscess all over the skin, then insert a needle below the area that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and have it tied with a double thread so that you can pull it out of the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or ligament of one of the two sides with a thread; and if you doubt whether the threads will pass through, insert another needle along the entire length of the first needle at the opening of the incision, and tie the threads in four parts; then crush the abscess so that the excess subsides, then crush the excess fat and leave what is tied; then apply a soft linen cloth moistened with wine and oil, then apply cures of tents and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in arteries and veins, they come in nerves when injured or from excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.
