And this often happens in the shoulder and the thumb and in all places where there are joints, and it is severe abscesses, and its color appears like the body's color, and it is in various positions with pain; and when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, but it is not completely within the body; rather, it lies beneath the skin; and it is quite silent from all sides, and it does not go forward or backward, up or down, and the one who is in joints should not be covered by iron: perhaps there would be contraction; and those who are in the head or forehead, press the skin with the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and hit its root; if it's large, support it with an onion, peel it off, then cut it open, stitch up the wound, and let it heal until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Large lumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; some are small and others are very large; I have seen a man who had two bellies that were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a slender root, and were split open, and continued to ooze moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed and found one to be 18 ounces, the other 6 pounds, and the work in the incision is such that if you look, you can see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and wet and has a delicate root; if it is covered with a large spatula, keep the cautery near fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 In the thigh, there often comes excessive bleeding, and if it overwhelms [you], then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient trembling with fear of the incision with iron, take well-made thread, tie it as we have said, and leave it for two days; then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the thread until it stops the bleeding, and causes pressure on the artery; and if the roots are large, be careful to cauterize it [the bleeding] entirely, but you can certainly cauterize half of it, then cure the wound, and be careful not to cauterize the tendon which is of dark color and poor sensation and lax appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to the treatment of the scrofula hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts forth
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of a boil comes from a wound or incision in the sifac (perineum), and it is on the abdomen and among some of the testicles, as happens in other routes, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is mentioned above, or from windiness; and if it is through the route of the sifac and the exit of the scrotum, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is through the intestine's opening, then it is more diverse; and when you press it with your hands, it repulses, and returns, and possibly becomes hardened, and grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and by great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and filled according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft and the workings are that you look to see if the appearance is from the blood of an artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary to let the treatment be.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, about the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 If the appearance is due to the intestine or bowel, you must instruct the patient to strain his anus, and extend himself straight, then bend down completely over the stool; then command him to push gently between your hands, then go around the side of the abscess with a spatula, then place half of the abscess above the large spoon; then tie it around with a strong thread or a strong cord made of tough silk firmly, and leave the patient's nose free from the tying; then open half of the abscess extended over the thread, and put your finger inside, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught in the thread, then untie it, and push the intestine out through the vent; and if you find the bowel, take it with the spoon, and scoop out the excess; and if the artery or vein oppose you, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and place them around what you have made in a cross that you pierce; then press the abscess in four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the side open until it can be removed by itself, and let the dead flesh rot by itself; or cut it when it becomes soft and can be removed, then cure what is necessary, and close the abscess as we have said; and drain the pus or moisture that you find, then cure the side of what is necessary, and suture the side.
dou chancre	two boils
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	In the division we said the resemblances of boils, and how to treat them with medicines, and how to remove the cure of iron; and we say boils occur in the flesh, and great caution is required in their treatment, and the ancients said that when boils are in a place where they can be shaved like boils that are on mammary glands, and in the thighs, and similar places, it should all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it should not be approached, because I never knew anyone to heal them; no one ever healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, it is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then let him heal if he has manifest repletion, then make the patient sick or healthy one league for the work; then pour your ointment or salve over the boil and shave all around, leaving nothing unshaven; and let the blood flow freely, and press well the place with your hand or something else, and if the discharge of blood makes you counteract against cutting the artery or vein, cauterize until the wound is staunched; then heal it with another medicine until it heals.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have already said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what way the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the treatment with medicine, and that which is treated with iron: only eclites are mentioned; one should not touch iron in these two resemblances: namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly thing; therefore, when you treat this dropsy resemblance called "eclites" with medicine, and the cure does not help, consider if the patient is weak or has other disease besides dropsy, such as sudden abdominal distension and similar things; in that case, do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong constitution, and he has no other disease except dropsy alone, and he is not too old nor too young, then act thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the attendant presses the abdomen pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the curved spatula as shown here:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And to cut through the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And it should be cautious when piercing the second part. It shall not be too deep so that it reaches the intestines when thrust in, and it shall not perforate; then examine if the hernia is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must cut through the third rib from above, straight down, over the navel; and if the hernia is due to liver disease, the incision should be on the left side of the third rib; and if it is due to the spleen, it should be on the right, and the patient should not lie on the incision so that the fluids do not flow towards the weak place; then pierce the skin with the instrument, and push, and withdraw your hand completely out of the wound to the level of the fingertip or a little beyond; then pierce the spleen until the instrument reaches the fluid level, which is the level of the liver, then draw it out, and insert this instrument in its shape as shown:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it resembles a silver needle of subtle material, and is made of linseed or light thread, and has an opening at the lower part; and one side has three openings; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes carve into a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the anvil, so when the instrument comes to the point where it meets the flesh, push the instrument upwards now; empty then either half or one third part, for if you empty too much in that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit due to the weapon, or they may faint, or approach death; but empty according to its strength, and according to what the patient's constitution and pulse indicate; then draw the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held for the caution that stops the bleeding which is above the sinew, as I have said, that you pierce in this manner; then start the instrument again the next day if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw a small amount of blood; do this every day, and take care not to leave too much blood but only a little.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and leave him much of water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bath and in the sun, and anoint with vinegar; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the wound
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born who have no foreskin or whose foreskin is small and not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary to open a spur at once, you must pierce with very thin splints according to this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 Then place the thin foreskin of wood on it, bind and keep it for 3 or 4 days until it wants to urinate, at which time the foreskin is removed and urine made, then put it back again; and in case there is no need because the urine that comes out does not leave the foreskin closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 The patient with a small hole (pertus) is treated with a plaster of clay (clo de plonc), as we have said, it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the hole in its place are blinded, for no one is born with the hole at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis up; and cannot have sex due to this because the matter cannot reach the marris, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the work is that the patient lies on their back with the head of the penis and the bottom in the same position as a pen, so that the foreskin can open in the middle, as needed; beware of blood flow that often comes, and if it happens, stop the bleeding by applying pressure to the affected area and treating the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this albatross appears on the penis, and it is an appearance of foul genitals; there are both malicious and non-malicious ones; you must catch them once a week with subtile ointment, pick and clean all of them, then put soft cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment on top, then treat with diaphinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the anus (albathe) is infected with pus and decayed, you must bring fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cauterized (copeit), and if the anus is swollen with the penis inside it, and has both parts within the skin and outside, first you must remove the part of the anus that is inside; and when it is sewn up, heal the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you are treating it together, the members of the shaft are not secure from being pierced, and darkness and corruption come into the shaft and where; all that is black and corrupted must be cut off, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from the rind of pompomegranate seeds and figs, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cauteries aid with these conditions together: that is, for bleeding and corruption; and if the members of the shaft are corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to bring or lead from the shaft a cane made of plank, and make the patient urinate around it; and when the hair comes out at the head of the shaft which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or occurs due to wound or abscess, then it is necessary to shave with an instrument, as much as the ligament is loosened, and release the members of the shaft from all sides; and if this is difficult to say, then it is necessary to shave with a spatula a little above the head of the shaft and the hair; then press gently between them, and put a thin linen cloth dampened in cold water underneath. It is not necessary for it to come out immediately.
de la circoncision	circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not simply the healing of wounds like other injuries; however, when we perform this work at our will and specifically on infants, it is necessary that we do the best work and make it as easy to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say circumcision for their children in the old days because it was not in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greater part of the masters and sages who performed circumcision around .i. day, and the strong, and in all cases a novice; however, the cowards because there are two pieces of cloth, and by chance if one above is cut off and it remains the one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it should be covered, and the pain is double; and in amputation, which is near the tip of the member, there is no assurance of healing; and in amputation of the nail by chance the iron escapes, ruins the work, and many times there is such a need for amputation that there is no need for amputation.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In the amputation made at the ligament of sinew, I have found the benefit of experiment, for the saw cuts equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. When you press your hand, you should make equal incisions all over; but ensure the thread is well tied around the skin; and the method of the first operation is such that you should make the child think, if it understands, that you tie only the thread around the rod, and then let it play in every way that you can; afterwards let it be between your hands straight, and reinforce the joint between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the tools; then push your hand to the rod and blow or draw, and pull upwards until the shoulder bone is extended; then clean it well of the filth that has accumulated there; then tie a double thread around the fracture; then tie one thread below the fracture to the other ligament; and hold it with the second ligature at the wrist and thumb, and break between the two ligaments, then quickly untie the knot and pull the head of the rod; then let the blood flow freely and let it pool, for this is the mucus; and sprinkle powder on it and powder made from cooked egg white tempered with rose water, confectioned with fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures as long as it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the strength for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and sharp, and they should be as large as the fists equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundification is when the vein within is cut open; then it must be stretched with your fingernail so that the wound festers over; and press it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, take tweezers, and then press.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If it lasts for three days and what is under the penis is swollen, let it be until the abscess subsides, and the wound scabs over; then press gently as you can move it, and keep away from the part of the penis, it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the limb with things beneath a wound of powder, as we have said or treating powders, and if you press too hard beyond measure, it will go above; then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or frozen mucus, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see it being retained because of a stone that is located at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over his knees; his feet should be placed on top, and he should extend his abdomen from the part above the back, and hold the patient as tightly as possible; and then the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above is compressed, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe," of which the following is the form: it should be made of thin silver light thread, like the feather of a bird; and its tube should be of a length of one and a half palms, and should be thin at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the issue of the urine is that you take a double thread, tie it to the head of a linen or cotton cloth, and push the head of the thread into the syringe; then tie off the excess linen and push it to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on the seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with oil moistened with olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the buttocks; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and the patient will feel it come up to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then the thread should be tied at the linen head, and the urine follows the linen, then remove the thread, and straighten the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Illnesses of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scratches or blood comes in the bladder, or pus is assembled there, and you see it exuding acids and medicines, do everything with the instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and if it has been pierced three times: one from one side, and another from the other, as you see; and the head of the verge [penis] becomes so swollen that the medicine cannot penetrate well, if we can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you wish to put your medicines in the bladder, place the head of the clyster [a device for administering liquid medication into the body] in the moisture, and draw out while it is inside; if you draw out the moisture with the clyster, then push forcefully while inside; the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clister [a medical procedure for administering liquid medication into the bladder] by which one clisterizes the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or iron, and the head is higher; beneath the breast or the ribs fall; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture that you use to plug the bladder, then insert it between the two breasts forming a good double string, heat the moistened part over the fire; then push the chief of the catheter into the urethra, then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisture reaching the patient; and when the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle, puncture it roundly; then push the strong thread through these holes, assemble the circle like a dial, put in what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and secure it in the instrument; do as you did with the bladder, press your hand hard until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the section on stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have told the difference between a stone embedded in the rain, and all the signs, and in which stone one should work in size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and it opens the urinary passage, and increases the pain of the patient's penis, and it pierces many times, and then twists; and from these jumps the foundations are weakened; and children's healing is light until they have 4 years, and it is very severe in the elderly, and it is a medium ailment for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes obstructs the search for the arrow.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take hold of the patient by the feet, turn and move him upside down so that the arrow comes out from the bladder and protrudes sometimes upward; then make him sit between your prepared hands, his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declined downward; then press and touch it; if you feel the arrow inside, hurry up to cut above the arrow.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall out when touched, moisten your left-hand index finger with oil if the patient is an infant, or use your thumb if the patient is an adult; and push it into its foundation, press and feel for the arrow, and when you feel it in your hand, push it towards the neck of the bladder; then press down on it, and push it out where you see it will cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and order him to extend his right hand upward and remove the skin below the scrotum in the part where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it, thus forming the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it should be placed between what is between the shoulders and the bottom, not in the middle but along the side of the left navige; and it should be straight above the stone, and your thumbs should be at the base or foundation, and the blade should be wide across and narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, the pressure on the thumb that is at the base, makes it jump out without much effort; and know that there may be this stone or it may have angles and edges: if it is grooved, it should be removed; and if it is soft, like a plum, and round, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then if there are angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you must strain it using pliers that are like a chisel at the tip to force the stone out; or you strike beneath it with a tool that is curved at the tip; and if you cannot deceive it in this way, expand the opening slightly, and scrape it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, strike the largest first against the bladder, then pound it, pull it out, and remove the smaller ones after.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it must be incised more deeply.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 Two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out constantly because the joint cannot be sutured; however, you must persist in trying to draw it out, or break it with pliers, as long as you can pull it apart piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, bind it, and cover it with a moistened linen cloth in oil and wine, or in olive oil and cold rose water and cold water to cool the abscess heat; then make the patient lie on his neck, and do not unbind the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you undo it (the bindings), wash it well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment defyfikon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses come into the wound and corrosions, and if the blood in the bladder freezes and is retained, preventing urine; then you should press down on the place, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder and pass through; then lift up the wound from pus and from rottenness and purulence, and help in every way that you know, until it heals; and you must tie all the herbs that you use on him to both legs, and apply the medicines directly on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the wound is small and it is closed from the penis and pierced with a lance, and urine cannot pass; you can cure it thus: cut it many times, excusing the cutting by this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod in the following shape and pierced at four angles into one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the stone's shaft, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the awl gently into the shaft; then turn the awl gradually towards the stone, until you can pierce the stone from another side; soon enough, urine will come out, then press your hand on the part of the stone remaining inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken and jumps out with the urine, the patient is cured; if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie the thread around the stone both below and above, then push the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone (of women)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that a stone is embedded in a woman, and if it ever occurs, it is a great trouble for the healer, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that there is the possibility that the woman is a virgin; and the second is that it cannot be found a woman skilled enough to reveal herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third way is that sometimes one cannot find a woman skilled in this craft of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of a woman is more deeply embedded than the stone of a man, therefore it requires a deeper incision, and great fear is present there. If such a situation arises, you must take a midwife who knows well, and if one cannot be found, then cast a subtle gaze; and present a wise woman in the art of women's life, or a woman who knows part of this craft, and command her to perform the incision of the stone; and pay close attention that the woman is a virgin: then she must put her hand into it and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should hold it with her hand, and you instruct her to place her hand or press her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is found, it must be moved little by little from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike above the bone in the root of the thigh near the junction of the bones, where it is moved and feels the bone in that part; do not move your finger above or below the bone, and cut it at first lightly; then push the rectum into the incision, if you feel the bone protruding so much that it can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: namely small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with grooves.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 know the appearances to know the solution.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the bone protrudes, place vitriol powder broken into it and hold for an hour until the bone is set; then return to your work as long as the pain remains, and have instruments as I told you in the removal of the bone for assistance in your work; and if the bone protrudes and it is the artery that was cut, place the powder on the wound and bind with tight bandages and do not start again, let the bone be and do not draw it out, lest the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the wound heals, then return to your work until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	Of a meaty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	An aquous hernia is nothing other than an accumulation of moisture or white pus, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called "white pus", and sometimes it is specifically within the egg's membrane, if one believes that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the bladder between the white pus we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and it spreads out this matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it happens due to a blow on the cheekbones, and this moisture can have various colors: either yellowish declining, or without red, black, white, or watery white, and it often happens; these are signs of recognizing this gathering, for if it is as white as we have said, it is an abscess that should be long like the figure of an egg, and do not open the cheekbones, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture within the cloth, it is abscesses that reason with part of the egg, and therefore it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin and the white syfac, it can be felt very well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, probe it entirely in all its depth, from which the form is as mentioned before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intromission (procedure), judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When we treat it with iron, the patient should be anesthetized according to our power and the fullness of his body; then make him lie on his back, on something a little higher, and place many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to stand on the right, and stretch out the rod to one of the two ribs near the shoulder; then take the spatula flat, and cut through the skin between them along its length until reaching the white syfac, and carefully scrape it thinly as much as our power allows; then pierce the syfac with water to a large hole and remove all the water, and put your fingers in, and stretch the syfur forward; and do not touch the shoulder, but only the syfur; cut all around it carefully, so that if you don't cut it well, the water will return; and if the egg bursts from your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the syfur treatment; then sew together the two levers of the shoulder into a stitch, and treat it as other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then you must bind the vessels that are suspended with caution to prevent bleeding; then cut the cartilage completely and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an ulcer is assembled in two parts together, know that these are the branches; if you touch the other part as you did the first equally, then draw out the blood, and put moistened linen in oil of roses into the wound; and put another moistened linen in wine and oil on it, and put on the two sides, and put over them double cloths, and tie it above all with string according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths and use thin linen according to this shape and sew them together at the middle of the belt, one of the shoulders takes hold beneath, and the other at the handle; and the other two sides should be tied together in the knot of the garter; and sometimes medicine is this branch of cautery in place of iron cutting, and it is that you take the cautery knife, touch the skin of the wounds, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the ulcer is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the pus with holes, and scrape the cautery hot against it:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cup in all ways that you can, until everything is heated; and ensure that fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more beneficial; and be careful of excessive bleeding, and beware of the works of cutting; and if anything opposes you, whether abscess or bleeding or something else, cure what opposes you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 If the patient is afraid and does not want to endure this work because of its horribleness, you should perform perforation, as I tell you; and it is that when you are certain, by the signs that we have said, that the pus is in the place, you make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below, all the way through the spadix large, and put the perforation along the length of the body; and let the holes be wide enough so that all the pus flows out; then put cotton over it and hold it, and allow the remaining pus to drain, until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not prevent the pus from flowing out of the wound, you must pour a feather or an instrument used for draining pus from edema, with the shape described before; and enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the pus returns, and is collected after 6 months or thereabouts, and when it is collected as before, and in this way the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the eyes
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the section of this remedy there is fear in many positions, which makes it seem useful to leave it; and I will tell you the work and the appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore I say that many abscesses come from the body, especially from the bowels; and this happens in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is by excessive sour and hot liquids that are spread to the kidneys or through percussion; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, but it is a severe abscess; and sometimes an abscess is swollen with fear and hardness, and of this color, and sometimes it comes from the artery or the inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it comes from the artery, it is known by the position of hot abscess when you press it with your hands, and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is made with swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the expression of touch on the fingers, and can well make the incision on this appearance, and on other things; it is that you cut the core of the hinge, then the egg is above, and the string goes out white, and delivers the suspender from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already rotten with these things born, then you must draw out the egg and crush it; if it is hard at the surface or inside the vessels, you must deliver all that softness and crush it thoroughly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the shell is on one side, you must crush it completely, and pull out the egg as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, apply the wound with dampened wool in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the eyes
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess covered by a swelling resembling a tumor with the softening of hinges; and the patient grows sick heavily when he goes; and the treatment for this illness is as dangerous as that described earlier, and nevertheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then push the suspension apparatus from below the shoulders to your hands, all the tools that are near the penis, and tighten them; then cut a deep groove with a sharp spatula across the testicles, until they are exposed, and then peel off from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then insert a double-threaded needle into it at the first place where the blood vessel appears, and tie it directly to the other end; then cut through the middle straight, according to the length of the body, removing the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with any other injury, so that no testicle sinks into one of the cheeks; for in this way there is no harm, and if all the testicles are exposed, it is necessary to withdraw the cheeks from all the testicles; so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the testicles, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the hernia
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The appearance of this injury arises from a section that comes or rupture, or the extension on the stomach in the area of the intestines; because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the kidneys; and this rupture is either of the bursting, or of the extension of it, and these two types of wounds occur for various causes: either by impact, or by jumping, or by falling, or by a fixed twist, and similar things; and the signs that it is of the extension of the rupture, are that it occurs little by little over a long time, and does not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the full, because the rupture follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is of the section of the disease, are such that they cause sudden pain at the beginning and abscesses appear different, close to the skin surface, which is due to the outflow of intestines and the body turning away from the disease.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines come out of the circles and are retained there, causing great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, which causes one to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the method of the work is that you instruct the patient to pull the intestine out with their hand inside the wound, if it can be inserted; then hold its neck between your hands, and separate the thighs; then place the knife above, and cut all the skin of the buttocks lengthwise; then insert your index finger into the hole created in the abdomen, as far as needed to open the wound, making sure that the eyes can come out; then remove the fatty layer that is underneath the skin, until the white fatty layer becomes visible from all sides; then insert your right hand inside the buttock, and place the white fatty layer on your left hand, and separate the abdomen towards the back; and instruct the assistant to stretch the abdomen upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and check with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped around or hard white fat, and if you find anything, push it into the abdomen; then take a needle with thick thread made of 10 threads, and insert it in the back part of the fatty layer, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the abdomen, then pierce the bones that appear from the thread, until there are 4 threads; then arrange them one on top of the other in a cross shape, and tie the fatty layer, as we have said which is underneath the skin of the buttocks, with a strong ligament of 2 parts; then wrap the bones with the thread, and tie them with 2 parts, so that no servants who carry it can enter; and place the ligament according to the first ligament length, 2 fingers long, and after these 2 ligaments leave the fatty layer which is underneath the buttock skin, a finger's width; and after that, according to the roundness that the egg carries; then pierce in the part that is under the skin of the buttocks, as far as necessary, and then bend it, as we have said above; then apply moistened linen in oil, and put it in the wound, and place the ligament that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes, the whites (of the eyes) are cauterized as we have said, after incision, due to fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this often happens, and leave the ligament until it chooses to slide off on its own; and if it delays in falling, rise it up with warm water, and put what we have said on it, until it slides off; then cure the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Of a meaty hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like the grafting of the eye, in this manner that you tie the vessels, above it lightly on the bottom; then press it together, and treat the abscess from what opens, until the vessels slide off; and heal it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.
