Sometimes it comes to rupture in the anus, as we have said, and do not remove any of the intestines at the opening; and if there is removal, it is little, and repair it every hour; and even so if it remains too long in this place, the wound or abscess grows until the intestines are removed; and this happens by the extension of the abscess which is in the anus, as we have said, for it is extended, then it becomes softened and swollen the area and opens; and the healing is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is healed by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands, then press the swollen area of the rupture with both hands according to the size of three fingers; and then extract the abscess that is under the skin that surrounds it, then take the fat and put it on the visible abscess; and press it firmly in the stomach, then tie both the visible parts of the abscess to the tip of the fat; and press the one and the other; then extract the tip of the fat, and do not cover or extend the egg nor any other thing, as I have told you in the treatment of the grafting of the intestines; then heal it by wound treatment.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you wound the flesh, if it putsrefies and heals the wound, let it be healed until it is sound.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swollen member has no appearance in the wound, and the fire cautery is applied here, and it is closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the swelling on the skin of the genitals
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the genitals becomes swollen in some men due to softening of the testicles, and it appears like pus; and when one sees it needs to be cured, you must make the patient lie down on his back, and strike the swollen skin on top of the natural skin; then bring together the two lips at a stitch, and if you see, first sew the excess skin swollen part in 3 or 4 firm stitches; then strike between the stitches, and the cure is like other wounds until it heals, and the thread the skin.
dou chastrement	The punishment (or treatment)
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Note that castration is discussed in our law, and I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary for only two reasons: the first being that the animals respond when asked about castration and their cure; and the second because we often have need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as cattle, sheep, pigs, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 Therefore, I say that castration is done in two ways: by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the castration done by attraction, we place the animal on a warm seat, until the scrotum becomes soft and relaxed; then we grasp them with our hand, holding them until they are repositioned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 For the branding of size: it is necessary that you mark the animal, and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the restrainer, and strike each testicle with a heated iron as needed; leave any small amount of skin and subtle skin that is on the balls, this type of branding is different than that which is made by attraction, because at attraction, something may remain accidentally from the scrotum, causing the animal to desire lust; then heal the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites (or intersex individuals)
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphrodyte is according to two types of humans: one in which there is an opening between the two scrotums as the figure of a woman's nature with hair and sometimes urinating in court.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And another way it is with women, and he places himself above them as with a rod and he copulates.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for men and women is that you copulate the adjacent genitals all, and treat them as other wounds are; in another way, from men whose urine jumps through the skin of the penis, it has no treatment.
de la tentigene	the tentigen
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 A swelling adjacent to the natural part is called tentigene if it is too ugly to see, and some women have such a large one that it is treated as a wound.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You must color the excess of the tentigene with your hand or some onions and lightly copulate it; do not go too deep that bleeding does not come out, then treat it with other medicine until it is healed. If another swelling arises at the husband's mouth and bursts forth, and resembles a cow, for this reason it is called an old disease "maladie kowee".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said before, and cure it until it heals.
de erratique	The cautery with fire instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 If the nature of woman is not perceived or it is small; and it is natural by birth or accident due to illness that comes about; or it is through false union, or through subtle or thick sperm, and is made completely in the marriage bed, or in the flanks, or elsewhere; and they must be prevented from conceiving, and giving birth, and accidentally having flow of fluids; and recognition of this is by the observation of the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the stoppage is near at hand, it appears to your eyes or right hand.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If it is through subtle sperm and it is near the liver, hurry and do as follows: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spread out her legs; then form the two livers, so that the subtle sperm is hard, and the stoppage is opened; then take wool, wet it in oil, and place it on the area, and have the woman rest at home every day, so that she does not strain.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the dislocation is hard and thick, you must cut it with a chisel resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is frozen, suspend it with a rope and strike; have medicines that stop bleeding such as hare's blood, dragon's blood, frankincense, together with much egg; then bring a broad plank to separate the wound; let it be long and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when in the marriage (union of a fractured bone) there comes frostbite, it must be covered in this manner, unless the abscess is incised.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an abscess swollen in the groin area, do not attempt to operate.
des emorroides	The diarrhea
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually do not require treatment, and when hemorrhoids become old they may thicken; and we have already said in the division their similarities, and the signs, and I will tell here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and thickenings, when they are completely in the groin area and cannot be felt, should not be cured with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those which are at the mouth of the groin, can be felt, are those which can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you must put the woman in a cold house, then boil the root of the hemorrhoid with tweezers, and apply the powder on medicines that stop bleeding, such as chalk and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding persists, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, grenadine bark, and ivy leaves, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it bleeds, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it does not bleed, you must apply blisters to the back and to the breasts without striking them with iron; then take linen, moisten it in the juice of onion or maror (a type of celery) with old wine, and apply it to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the abscess rests, you must treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough crust, so it must be covered as I have said in the previous text; and then you must continue treating it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many forms of abscess come in marriage, such as boils and painful abscesses, herpes, sores, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have said in the division (of this chapter).
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is necessary that I say in this treatise about the abscess which comes in marriage, which is not one of those that stick out; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it heal as much as the pain is alleviated; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have two small stools or he leans, and support his back and legs at the parts away from the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a strong thread; then bring the boil towards the right side, and introduce the instrument used to open the abscess, of which the following form will come; and it is necessary that when you wish to introduce this instrument, that you pierce the tip first to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters within the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloth, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it must put the horn of the instrument above, and mark the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess is opened and handled with a soft hand, it should be covered with lint at the top; and when the boil is empty, you must put in the wound moistened linen in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the linen strip from the wound to the tip of the thumb, and place above the thumb and on the net clean linen soaked in vinegar or malvaceae which have been cooked; then treat it after two days with ointment following this, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the thumb and the wound by suppository of vinegar and honey, and then of vinegar or longis Aristolochia roots which have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is healed in the sea moss, it's necessary that you refrain from iron heating; rather, treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 First of all, the midwife must recognize the figure of natural childbirth and the signs when you see the woman after labor, and she desires to push out the afterbirth: then hasten the infant to be born; understand that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it issues from under the head, followed by the placenta, and when you see these signs, it's necessary to gently press her belly, so that the infant comes quickly; for when it descends towards the head, it follows with it, and the afterbirth is purged from its superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 It happens sometimes that something falls upon the feet, or the body or shoulders, or the hands, or upon the stomach or head, and by chance they are turned around in a bad way on the neck or elsewhere; therefore it is necessary for a balm to be wise and skilled in these matters, and to avoid errors and deceptions, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out from under its head naturally and the woman gives birth with difficulty and her strength is weak, make her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then apply to her nature oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then put the midwife between her hands the small spatula of which this form is:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And cut the second rib, and strike at its tip until the moisture within is expelled; and grasp the woman's belly as far as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must cleanse the woman with fennel juice and oil of cumin; afterwards make her take a laxative made from castor oil, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: in this way, the child will be born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out, you must gently pull them back bit by bit; and if they cannot be put back, lay the woman on the chair, lift her legs high; then tilt the chair onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not move when tilting it; and if the hands cannot go back in, and the child is dead, strike the hands with the knife that has been placed here before, extract the child, and pull them back equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 The emergence of the child from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes up from its feet, you must push it up; then gradually turn it until it is straight; then take hold of its feet and stretch them out gradually.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 If it can jump to such knees, let him command to catch it, and make it sneeze with disgust; if it leaps away, may it be as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as much as we said, if you turn it little by little until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if it does not come as we have experienced, say that she takes mustard of great heat, oil of cumin, and melted resin, and grind all in a mortar; then put the nature of woman inside this ointment, and apply it to the area and let it stay for a while; then make her sit in hot water up to her chest; when she is softened below, let her wear an amber collar, and apply it to her, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the chair, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and press gently on the belly because the infant jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's birth upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, place it on its back with its hands folded close; then lay it on its neck and let the feet hang down, and make it lie on the bed; fold its hands again and then take hold of them above its stomach, and push its hips out below until it is prepared for delivery; if the child does not come out, take hold of its legs and turn them forward, then turn its stomach upward, and put your hands in; pull the child little by little; and command the woman to take ahold of herself as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The birth of the child is coming out one hand's breadth wide.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to devise a method to return the hand: if you cannot return it, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed and spread out her legs; then bring the moxa (moxa stick) that I have mentioned earlier; if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, and devise a method to return the hand; and pull the child according to its natural shape, and make her vomit, and command her to take ahold of herself as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	The issue of the child on its neck, and he has spread his hands, and his face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the ball (assistant) holds his hand, then turns it slowly and gently, and when it becomes even, put a mustard poultice of alum and oil on it as we have said, then command him to move it slowly; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to grasp it; and make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same manner, all must be reduced.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When the afterbirth comes in this way all around (the baby), if you grasp the afterbirth with your nail, until the moisture is emptied; and if it swells up on her face and neck, strike it so that it is not retained, and let the afterbirth die; then push the child in as much as you have to, and command the woman to grasp (it) once: then let it come out gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four; and it is not strange, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 These are strange things that do not live unless named; I know these, which multiply and are desired by the one who devises them, who is tied to filth; and sometimes they issue out naturally like a mouse's offspring, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 If they issue forcefully, then the cure is as we have said, and let the bailiff be subtle, and do quickly and easily what it does; and do so as it is worth moving to salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six, or more up to fifteen; and all of them are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows this because similar things may happen; so do as is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat a woman with a dead child or an unborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work by hand; then you must know if the woman is of good virtue and has no accident or fear of death; the woman should be laid on her back with her hips inclined downwards and her legs raised; and the minister touches her twice, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated for the removal of the child; then anoint the wife's mouth with moist oils mixed with musk and fenugreek seed and linseed; then oil the hands of the minister with these oils and musks; then gently push in the mouth, then seek the place where the twins are, if they are suitable for this purpose, and beware that the membranes surrounding the child are exposed so that it can descend onto its head; then push the twins into their places, either in the vagina, neck, mouth, palate, under the beard or near the navel, or by the sides, and if the removal is at the feet, push or pinch and in the middle of the ribs; and the right hand must hold the twin, and put the forearm between the left hand, and gently push with the entire hand into any of the places we have mentioned, until it reaches an empty place; and this is the shape of the twin:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then push against the other bone, where necessary if you need to extract it, so that the extraction is even; and then make it equal by moving from both sides to bring them together, causing them to move apart, and the bones should be fitted together tightly as shown in the following figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if a part remains, you press oil from one of your fingers and insert it in that part, pulling the other part; and if no part remains, place the bone higher or at another level, and continue this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be returned due to tightness, you should wrap it up in a cloth until it comes out completely; then break it at the joint of the foot or the heel, and do the same for the other hand and feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow at the exit, or if it has a swollen head assembled, you must push the pointed spatula between your fingers, and make the head and extract the swelling; or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the chapter after this takes its form with the tools; and in the same way do for the breech if it is naturally large; and then pull the bones apart with tongs, and if the head leaps out and is held by force, it should be cut, as necessary, until the swelling that is further inside comes out; and if it cannot come out, break it up into pieces where you can. And if it is swollen in the abdomen or under the ribs, you must pierce it until the swelling comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, its removal will be easy and redirecting it to the mouth of the wound will be easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is protruding from the abdomen or the anus, you should pull it back into place wrapped in a cloth over the hand; and when pulling the abdomen or the anus, move the moisture that is present there; and if other members are dislocated and remain, press the ball of the hand fully into the incision of the hernia, and pull it out; then insert a finger or two, and pull it further; and if the hernia is narrow due to an abscess that has come, you should not try to force it, but instead provide moist and greasy substances; and apply emollients, and use hot, softening and moistening substances.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on the side, and you can make it straight, do as we have said in the case of a live birth; and if there is no power to do so, draw it out piece by piece, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 When you have done this, do as we have said in the case of abscesses that come in the marriage (womb); and if there is discharge of blood, it should be stopped by strong pressure, and other treatments applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom the child inside was dead, then consulted another on this and revived the child.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in the groin, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to putrefy greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the healing, and for a long time I considered it, but could not stop the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed strong adhesive plaster on it, and after some days another bone appeared.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, since the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I wish to treat the wound, and pull out many bones as long as the woman is in the best position; and the woman lives for a long time thus, and then after a little while there is some pus from the wound; and I do not remember this chapter except because when masters find an unusual thing which they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to put the arm back in its place (or socket)
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the first sentence to translate:
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The shoulder head dislocation tool should be more subtle than the restrainer, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the rod should be wide, and the edges of the handles must be, and a palm and a half in length; and between the two limbs there should be two alignments of the same rod, which are tightened in one and the other, half a palm long or an inch more; and these two alignments are placed in the mouth of the marris for opening when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, resembling something more subtle and lighter, should be made of rod of ebony or boxwood, similar in appearance to pliers; and have two alignments for the shoulders, as you see, a palm in length, and two fingers wide; and when you are about to open the marris with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then place the two alignments aligned together in the marris, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then move your hand with the entire instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the marris, until the woman does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These tools are all covered and have similar appearances; and when the blacksmith has equipped them, they work more quickly, and higher for humans because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Never disdain the tool that you have not equipped, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold back her lochia, and then make her vomit with emetics, and hold her hands at the mouth and nostrils; and if she jumps due to this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take the suppository and use a cup or basin, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the deceased woman, such as rue, anise, chamomile, calaminthe, centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over fire; then put a cup or basin from the pot and hold it under the woman's nose, and keep it there until the vapors enter the woman; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient suddenly jumps up.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment and does not heal, instruct the midwife to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or musk-scented balm of aloe, then apply it to nature and wait; when she has found it, take it and stretch it gently straight, so that the baby does not cry during extraction; but it must be moved gently to the right and to the left, and then draw; it will come and expel itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the baby has been stretched, we have said the treatment for expulsion and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not do this as we have said, make sure you do not pull; but let the one who is at the mouth of the baby be tied to the woman's thigh, then clisterize with ointment tetrafarmaçon; he will close it again and it will expel itself; however, when she returns if she brings a bad smell to the stomach and the head of the patient, it will inflame the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary to use suitable fumigations for this condition; no one of the ancients has tested fumigation with dill and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for retaining the flowers and the afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it looks like glass resembling a dog's head, and the soft part is placed in its nature, and the shoulders are large above the fire; and let there be fumigation over the coals, and the taint until it is spoiled, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce through the bottom
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced but rather stopped up with some subtle silica; therefore, it is necessary to open that silica at its proper place, and do not pierce it with a sharp splint, and guard the membrane so it is not touched; then put moist linen on top of it in wine and oil, and cure it with an ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will reopen, place a plank on it and leave it for many hours, and it should be taken off when the child wishes to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this sudden swelling of a wound or abscess occurs; it must be covered: whether treated, as we have said, with the poultice of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	Of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come below the foundation are nodules and grow from below the foundation or in the space between two parts, which may have one fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it is opened and moisture awakens pus or a thin boil, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; they are recognized by those who see or feel an emission or windiness in the patient, and occasionally there is a jump of urine.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder and halfway up the penis; they reach the knee joint and the ankle.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And so one recognizes the fistula persisting at its base, and not persisting: it is that you insert your finger into the fistula or its base, and push in a fine awl of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If it has twisting, then insert a fine probe of wood or horse hair until you feel the probe or the hair at your fingertip; and if you do not feel it, and there is no pus discharge or wind or worm, as we have said: know that it does not perforate; hurry in the treatment.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And if the fistula extends to the bladder or leads to the flow of urine, if it gushes forth, and cannot be sealed with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated until the joint of the shin, then the probe comes to its place; if there is no twisting and relief of pain around it, it is that it has already burst, and no medicine nor salve by ointment is useful for it; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish men who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In a woman who is neither a persian nor old, in hope of health through fire, as I have experienced, the patient lies between your hands on her back; and lifts her legs up to her thighs, and has her thighs inclined towards her stomach; then push a tent of iron or plank, if there is any curvature, until you know where the dislocation comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels pain around the base, it is necessary that you push your index finger there, then if it goes through the abscess or flesh, it will be discovered where the dislocation is; and when you feel between your fingers the bone or cartilage, then know that it is a dislocated shoulder; do not try to move it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One must say that some can be well healed, but it happens rarely; and the help one gives, it is when one heats the cautery subtle according to the width of the fistula, as was said before; and push all hot in the fistula, until it comes out from the foundation; and do this two or three times, until you know that these charred parts are burned, which are similar to a feather of an eye; and then cure with tents made moist in butter, until those charred parts disappear; then cure with ointment soothing and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters and does not pierce to the point which is at the foundation, and between your finger and the tent put a thick covering of fat or soap, and you see the fistula under this cover; then take hold of the beginning of the fistula, and push towards the tent, and then the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the end of the tent; and the tent will be released, and charred; then separate those charred parts that resemble a feather of a bird, and there remains nothing.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the bone pierces through [the flesh], and cuts into you or the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine ointment.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The fire cautery brings about two good things: the burning of these attached charms, and the stopping of blood flow and removal of moisture; then it heals wounds moistened with mulled tents or in a pot filled with coarsely ground chaff, until the lees settle down, and the charred bones are buried in the bowel; then the wound is healed by ointments made of hard charcoal, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is restored, it becomes healed and will not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the full depth of its foundation and is removed from the body, push it in with your thumb or foundation, and investigate it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent, and between them is the cloth or the silk or charms, which are close to being pierced, there should be no more than faith and hope through the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize as we have said, or you drive in until bottomed out, or if it swells, apply tents and heal as first described; but do not go too deep, so as to not cover the foundation-holding material, and let the discharge come forth willingly; then heal, as was said before; perhaps it will become healthy. Then remove that contaminated char in the wound, as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound, and keep the fistula away from the foundation: it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas occur in this manner: and it is when you press the tent (or "tumor") into the fistula, and it is where the bottom touches the skin above, then take a pointed probe with this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert one twisted thread into two, and insert the sheath along the whole thread into the fistula until it reaches its end.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is in the margin of the bottom inside, then draw out the thread from that piercing, pressing your finger or base there; and take hold of the tip of the thread, and bring together the two holes (or "wounds"); and hold one against the other, and leave them for a day or two; and tighten it occasionally, until the threads catch those hard things that are between them, and break through; then heal the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula is not pierced, then pierce it in any way possible, as long as it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it should not be covered too deeply and then treated until it heals as we have said.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The form of the splint spur, from which a fistula is made, is very sharp on one side and cuts; and blunt on the other, because one should not strike where one should not strike, as you see here.
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 There are two types of emorrhoids: either they are within the foundation, like grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and blood is present in them, and there is one or more, and they are bent away from the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are bent are moist, and there may be a little moisture, a little bitter juice, or a little blood, and have the color of the body. The cure for those located within the foundation is to command the patient to strain in order to urinate in chambers until the foundation emerges, and then the filaments can be seen; if you hurry, catch them with pliers or hold them with your nail, then strike at their roots; and if the filaments cannot be held due to moisture, take a cloth or cotton, or a piece of camelid wool; wrap them around and squeeze, then strike, and sprinkle some hot powders on top as a substitute for cautery; or you may cauterize them as described in the chapter of cautery, care for other cures until it heals; if the foundation does not emerge, clisterize the patient with a biting and harsh clisterium to clean the area where the foundation is located, so that it can emerge openly. The patient will feel better if the filaments are free from the foundation, and it is easy to cure them when you catch them with pliers or with your nail, then care for them as we have said, until they heal, and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You should apply the stitching in this manner: Take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, then turn both ends of the thread under the needle, making sure it is wide; tie the knot, pull the thread taut, remove the needle, and do the same for all the others. Leave some space for excess blood; then put a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or wax on the wound foundation, and place it there, and tell the patient to rest; then leave it until it drains, and when it stops draining, cure it with ointment and other treatments until it heals.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the fire or foundation   (This line seems to be incomplete or missing some part)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying of the intestines due to fire and by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and the medicine has no effect.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You should scrape the skin on top of a splinter or nail with a spatula or fingernail so that it does not get wet; then treat it until it heals as necessary; and if it cannot heal, you must shave more strongly than before, making sure it is clean and scraped off; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	The trembling (or shivering)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A scab is a small appearance that grows near the body and goes deep; sometimes it finds the flesh and feels like death frost, and comes all over the body, more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the treatment is that you take a feather of an ostrich or a strong goose feather and put it on the frost, making the circle of the feather encircle the frost all around; then turn your hand over the whole feather until you cut through all the frost, and place it deep, and scrape off the frost from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do as with a dog or iron chain of this shape, and be subtle inside and pull it out from above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, for fear of the thumb; and press it hard. If you see, then cauterize the swelling, as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the plaster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes plasters of silver or arsenic, or melted beeswax or lard, are made; and sometimes such small and large instruments are made according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, when administering to children or weak and suffering individuals, the plasters should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large plasters is as follows: wide or flat, with the belly tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And it should have an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the shoulders inside pierced; and on one of the sides there are two holes, and in the other one; and fill the belly with the medicine of a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be some space; then put strong thread through each hole, crosswise or circular, and assemble the belly like a bag; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then bind (it); and this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg yolk, or similar thing, then gently put it in; then the ministers squeeze it with both hands until it is completely viewed, then remove the clistere, and tie the patient's legs to the parchment, and if the medicine appears, hold it as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it is more aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply a plaster for the disease of stomach decay, and the medicine is hastened to heal, then continue it until it becomes healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoid is founded on an abscess or fistula, it should also be treated with the same subtle rectal cleansing method used for a child; and this is the form of the subtle rectal cleansing where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 Things by which wounds are made are through stone impact, sword cut and knife, or lance or fist, or similar things; or those that are made according to the body's laws, such as a wound on the neck, or head, or belly, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will start with the simple wounds of the head, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound or injury occurs where the bone is not broken, be careful if it is due to an arrow or similar things, and the skin is torn completely and the wound is large; doubtfully there is abscess formation: make it drain immediately from the head itself even if blood comes out of the wound; and the patient should avoid excessive intake of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not want to drain, reduce the food, do not drink wine, nor eat meat; and place on the wound, if there is abscess pus present, cotton moistened only in rose oil or in stiptic wine; and if there is no abscess pus, place on the fresh wound that has all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder (I will say a little more about this later); and if fire has moved it, place some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	If the wound is large like that of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be closed with stitches, then join them by suturing, as I will say for abdominal wounds, by suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone and festering but cannot be held together with only one finger, strike it; then treat the wound with medicine, replace tough flesh instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods such as cooked meat (e.g., beef and wheat), pulses (e.g., peas), and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if the rotten flesh or skin cannot be pulled away from the bone, strike it all and throw it away, then treat it; and if there are arteries in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped without a ligature and cannot be staunched by medicine, ligature them, and if you find the dislocation, tie it with thread; and if that does not work, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy; it is that you put this powder which solidifies as soon as the flesh has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and grind it finely, then apply it to the wound, press firmly until it airs well and joins with all its blood; then bind it well, and leave it to heal, if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes this is done with chalk only, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has not healed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has opened the wound, indeed it should be so, do not put this powder on it; but place some remedies digested, or poultice made from barley flour and water and honey, until it exudes pus; then heal it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the bone break comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you afterwards about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes or it is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it's nerves, there is no other device but to let the healing occur naturally and not put anything restricting, as this harms nerves and causes them to recede; and do not place anything cold on the wound, as the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as washed alum in mild water, mixed with rose oil, and cooked in the same way, and other similar stones according to this method, and immediately moistened.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, cut it and bind it with bands, until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.
