And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, pierce or cut lower; if the arteries are cut, bleeding ensues, so stop it, lance it, and cauterize as necessary; if the spine of the neck is cut or the veins, keep them guarded so that the meat goes up, not touching the throat but reset it according to its natural figure; then pull gently, leave for some days, then treat with discarded onions until it heals; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, break it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and leave those you cannot have until the wound festers, and dissect and align the exit; and if the wound is fresh, apply powder as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife wound, and the wound is deep, examine if air bubbles come from the wound as the patient lies still: then you should know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep and the blood flow is fresh at its origin, do not put powder on it immediately nor bind it for the blood that will not clot and return to the heart, and let the patient die; but apply attractive ointment and apply it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound 3 or 4 days, or more; no spasms, bad tremors of heart nor any signs of pain will come; and when you see good conditions, then know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat the wound and other treatments while it is still healthy; and if it cannot heal, then open it and know that there is a fistula; cure it as you should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, deep, or on the back, then cure what is in front of it; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, powder it; and if it penetrated into the bone and fractured pieces, treat the wound and pull out the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound heal by itself, aligning the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgments are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The rupture of the stomach (or abdomen)
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The first sentence to translate is: "The ruptures of the abdomen are large, medium, and small; from a large wound, the intestines sometimes protrude once, or the intestine's nerves, due to which they require intrusion; and the suturing is more difficult, and often a small wound is worse than a large one, because they put more pressure on the intestines when replacing them if not placed layer by layer; because the intestines inflate suddenly when feeling cold, they shrink more, and for this reason, medium wounds are better, because one must reset the intestines to their place rather than others. And know that the abdominal rupture is in four ways: the two common suturings occur in the abdominal suture, and the sutures of other body parts and two other specific ones are common for other wounds; however, they are more similar to the abdominal suture, and I will say one and explain each.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is protruding, it is easy to treat, which can be done in one of two ways: either because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a damp cloth only with hot water, or cook it in hot squill and cedar and pepper, and massage the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes make this vinegar-restraining, and it will be moist so that it can be drained to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling dispersing, moisten the intestines with hot or cold water and bitter vegetables, because in this way the entrance is quickly closed; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision at the instrument with which you cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is to be moist so that it can be drained, and we should not cut too much of it without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: cut from within in the hollow and do not turn over, and look at this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines fall out, put it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you have the power to do so, for this is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; if it is in the lower part of the belly, raise the head and feet higher than the parts below, and in the same way, if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, take care that the injured part is higher than the other. In this way, you should attend to both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use what fits you, then take a compassionate person who touches the entire wound with their hand and presses the edges together; this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you take one or more needles, depending on the size of the wound, then leave a space at the head of the wound and sew in a strong thick thread; pierce the two skins with the two hairs beneath the skin, which is under the skin inside, as far as you make it pierced from that part, and bring together the four heads three times; then tie a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound again, then leave a space, and sew again; then bind the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop until the entire wound is tightened; and the needles should be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, because very thin needles puncture all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be medium-sized; and do not push the needles too far away from the flesh and skin, so that they do not open or widen the wound before it is sutured; and then bind the heads of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and tie tents or cloths on the heads of the needles to hold them, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because a single needle or two supplementary stitches are enough in this case, and it is that you bring together the two skins and the two hairs beneath the skin with one needle having a medium thick thread; and when you have sewn all four together, remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner of sewing clothes; and leave space between each stitch the thickness of a minor egg; this suturing is called "home", and I sutured a wound that a man had or abdomen, which was stabbed with a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and it exposed his intestines about two palms, and the wound was inside the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I put the intestine back after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was stitched shut for 15 days, and it healed, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where no such thing or any medicine was found; I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Here I shall tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and pass it through from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the skin straight through, put the point where the skin or suture is that you have pierced, and make it go through from the other side of the inner part to the outer; and the meaning of this stitching is that you sew like a tailor sews fur, and leave one side once, then take up the other, until the stitching is all complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of suturing, as Galen himself describes, is when two parts are joined together naturally, and one end of the suture is attached to another end in this manner: stick a needle or end of the thread near the mirror side and pierce only that spot, leaving the other two ends; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part to the inner, through the two ends left behind; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner, in the two other thread ends that are on the opposite side; and this is the method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens said this word and it is true, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, each having thread; one needle should be pushed from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when the wound is within the belly, the suturing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgement of the wound is similar to that of other wounds: it is when you find the fresh wound full of blood, just as the arrow has moved it, then you replace the intestines and the fat; then put on a healing powder, and if the arrow has moved it, apply any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and sew up each hole, and bind the sinews, and the muscles; then heal the wound as you would other wounds, until it becomes healthy; and if you do not have medicines, immediately put on, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and stir it two times a day until it becomes healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need other medicine in more cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound spreads to the principal members, then you must moisten light linen in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the injuries, and beneath the bandages; and if there is pain or pus in bulges, and this often happens, then clisterize with black wine, and likewise if the pus comes up to the intestine; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when perforated, and this is due to the inflammation of the veins that are there, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the shinbone (zirbe) jumps out of the wound, you should reset it in its original position while it is still fresh; and if it becomes old and turns black or green, then you need to cut away the black part, ensuring no more blood comes from the veins or arteries; then grab what's between the tendons, and hang the two heads (chiés) hanging below the wound on each side to straighten the extraction when the shinbone falls out, and the wound will swell.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, as I have seen a man who was pierced or wounded by a lance; the wound was near the stomach and became ulcerated and turned into a fistula, with faeces and gas coming out of it; I treated it according to what I knew, and did not stop massaging it until it healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I see it sutured, I feared the patient had pain in his stomach; and there was no pain, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experienced men said that when a small wound is in the intestines, it should be tied in such a way: take deep breaths with large mouths, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the breath has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches out; and then strike the head, and hold it so that it cannot slip apart, then put another breath after in the same way until the wound is completely captured; and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head of an internal organ swells in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, it can be sewn up with a fine thread made from the intestine of an animal, like this: take the end of the thread from the animal's intestine, which should be very sharp; then tie it to the head of a linen thread twisted together; then insert the thread into a needle, and stitch the intestine and pull it through; and in this way of sewing, there is no remedy except by faith and hope; if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the greater intestines, there is no trick or healthiness, unless by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or ...
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows, is universally called "fistula," and likewise when it swells and bows out.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is according to truth a hard and white nodule or swelling, where there is no pain, and it is as swollen as the feather of a bird; sometimes it clears up in a clear spot, and other times it thickens; sometimes it is shallow, and other times it is quite deep; I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is not healthy except by one of the nine causes: namely, due to the smallness of the blood or body; or due to its malignancy; or because there is hard flesh within, and above the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or it has too much swelling; or the bones are broken, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in treatment; or because the corruption is a type of pestilence; or due to the property in the region being slow in digestion and late in health, and fleeing by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the medicines for treatment in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you the cure for a fistula that is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or to the skin, or intestines, or bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and when it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all these fistulas of this kind are difficult to cure, except for labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I said and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it recognized, take a tent of wax or iron, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; and if the fistula is twisted, look for a thin probe of wood, because the splinters bend around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has holes and you cannot find it well with probes, fill it with a clisterium through one of the openings, because the moisture can pass from one opening to another and cleanse it; then pierce it skillfully to your ability, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve inside, and if it is complete, ask the patient about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and where he feels it; and when you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from jointure, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I said, then cut according to what I said, and remove the false tissue and the rotten matter that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well perforated in a straight place, then you must cut completely, as much as you can, then put moist probes soaked in medicinal wax into it, and push them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains inside; and then put fresh char ointments on it, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve does not cause you trouble or problems with major limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, let it be cleaned until all corruption is removed, then treat with healing herbs until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and turns bent as before, know that you are not yet at the font: expose it and clean it thoroughly until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep and you cannot reach it, know that there is no other means but to let nature take its course; if there is a small corrupted bone and you can extract it with pliers, remove it using an appropriate instrument for the purpose, and if there are many bones, extract them all, do not leave any; if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, strike moisture and heat and relieve the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove [the foreign body] within an hour, put something irritating purgative on the wound around the bones and let it stay until the flesh is rotten around the bone, and then the bones will be easier; and if it's a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, press only on the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much corruption and it reaches the marrow of the bone, you must be careful and cover it entirely up to the corruption, and then let it heal until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause that caused materials to come to the leg, and it developed a large abscess without any cause for it to burst; but they foolishly operated on the abscess so much that the abscess opened up, and a lot of materials came out, and it became a fistula, and many pus-filled corruptions came from within his body; and for two years many people tried to cure him, but there was no skilled hand in the art, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they were using, and the corruption that flowed out of the pus with great force; and the young man's body became red, and he had a citron-colored complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I sewed up one of the wounds, and then searched for all the wounds, and found that some were coming together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Then I hurried and sewed into one of the wounds until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced; corruption was coming towards the bone from inside; what appeared to me as the rotten part seemed to be the only corruption, except for that which I left; and I began to heal the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not suture it; then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found continuous corruption in the bone, and removed it, and then stopped sewing; and I tried to suture the place, but could not do so until I sewed around a palm of the bone, and pulled away all the surrounding tissue, then I healed it with medicines again; and it became healthy and sutured quickly, and there was no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the evacuation, it often bled, but it healed completely, and a hard cyst grew in place of the bone, and it was well-positioned with no harm or counteraction at all, neither to the side nor to the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 If a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated as follows: take thread, and bind it to the open end of the bone, and command someone to extend it upward; put another thread of linen larger than the first thread over the cyst that is away from the bone, and bind it so that you draw the corrupted cyst downwards, and uncover the cyst at the place where you wish it to be, so that the cyst does not bleed the healthy cyst; put charcoal or a piece of wood under the bone to protect the corrupted cyst; and be as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and stay for another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, you must uncover all the flesh; then put fire under it, and then make the instrument to be on one side of the corruption for as long as the length of the corruption; and if the corruption is at the joint, strike the corrupted joint, and hold the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other way but to cut it; and if the corruption is at the tip of the finger or toe, this is a difficult thing, but nevertheless you must examine the corruption, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but let neither the vein nor the nerve hinder you; and know that there are many types of instruments for covering these bones, according to the type of bone and its appearance, and its thickness and subtlety, and size and smallness, and hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the diseases; and think of the instrument that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	cautere de
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head may fall out due to either an internal or external cause, and when you have applied the cure for this corruption by means of medicine but it brings no benefit, you must cover that member up to where the corruption occurs; otherwise, the patient will suffer from death or a worse fate, namely the failure of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, appearing as if it is burned by fire, and after becoming black, the corruption of the member spreads from one member to another and affects the entire body; hasten to cover [it], and if it is due to the bite of certain venomous animals like the sea scorpion, viper, or similar, cover the head and do not give it any space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the wrist, press it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, press at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and thus you should do when the corrosion comes or pus: if it comes at the first joint, press after the next joint; and if it comes in the foot, press the entire foot; and if it climbs into the leg, press at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to tire the patient to death; and the method of pressing or soothing the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister one of the ligaments below, and another minister the other ligament above, and you push out the flesh that is between the two ligaments with a large spatula, until the bone is exposed; then press or soothe, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the lard does not touch healthy skin, and bring another injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And when bleeding of blood comes as you work, cauterize the area immediately, or apply certain powder restraining ones; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a suitable rope and heal it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to one man: he had a black spot resembling a fire burn, and that corrosion first appeared in his foot, consuming all of the foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered the foot with copper and was healed; and for a long time after, the corrosion returned to his hand or to his toe, and it came to me, and I applied healing substances after the purification of the body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he asked that I amputate his hand, and I refused because I had hope of stopping the matter; and I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, as the strength of the man was weak; and he lost all hope, and returned to his land, and covered his hand with copper and was healed; and I have never heard this story except for this reason: it is done otherwise when needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess appears in a charred place and remains for so long that it causes a large swelling of the body; then it breaks open and goes, and the place heals over as a wound does, like a knight's armour; and the skin that is on top is as thin as linen cloth, and will not reach the bone or nerve, and such disease is called "san," and is not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so large that it reaches the bone in full, it is called "fistula"; and the skin should be cut all around, just as one would cut linen cloth; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	1. And if the skin hardens and the corruption is not complete, and the flesh is thick with char, cure it thus: check if the breasts are large, and the sore that is in it smells badly; then clisterize with Egyptian medicine made as follows: take asafoetida, oil, and litargire equally, cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take according to your need, make into water and honey, and apply the clisterium to the breast, and press it out; leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is drained and the pus is removed; and at no time is the clisterium applied with vinegar when the Egyptian medicine is not present, and take vine ash instead, pour water over it, then stir and apply as a clisterium, until you know that the breast is clean; and if the patient cannot endure it, or the Egyptian medicine and the vine ash are not available, apply water and honey or mead, which has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine strengthens the blood; and when this is done, and you have confidence that the breast is well cleaned, apply to it whatever medicine that makes pus grow in it, and take emplastrum definitive and oil of roses, mix them with wine; or apply other medicines and unguents, whose properties I have mentioned earlier; and if the wound of the breast is small, and the clisterium applicator cannot enter it, widen it a little with iron, and apply an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, enough to be widened; and if the wound is too large, make it smaller and only allow the level or the clisterium to enter, and if the pus that comes out smells badly, press down or press it lower.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the bowel is fully dilated, do not let it be engorged with flesh; and if you cannot cover the belly under it as you see, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest point possible, for when the bowel is fully dilated, do not let it be engorged with flesh and if you cannot cover the belly under it as you see, arrange it like this: let the bowel move slightly downwards and do not leave anything from the bowel; take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and place a linen cloth over the entire wound; then apply force in the direction of the perforation in the belly, which is larger than the first, then immediately bind it with another cloth according to the size of the perforation, and place it on the perforation of the wound to align the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth except after several days; and he who is on the perforation in the belly, frequently removes to remove the bowel, and knows whether it comes from the bowel, whether venom or pus or too much, digested or indigestible; and keep watch if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the perforation of the wound, know that the bowels have healed and are approaching health; then uncover it in the morning or the third day, and when you uncover the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the binding.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast sags down improperly after many days, know that the breast will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison spreads after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And for those whose flesh swells in their wounds and those who act contrary to it; and if the breast swells indigestedly after many days, know that the breast does not heal itself; and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is spreading out, apply drying medicines with dry substance and wet virtue, such as oil of roses, for there is much vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine; take oil of roses, and make it with rose oil, and equal amounts of old wine by volume; then let it steep and use it; and when oil of roses is not present, you may take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them together, powder them over the honey while it is on the fire; and then rub the cloth into the honey, and place it on the breast, and sometimes administer long Aristolochia root, which is similar to flour and chalk; and use simple or compound medicines: grind them, make them into a powder, and put it over the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the wound is deep and not cured by this treatment, know that the corruption has spread throughout, and makes an impression in the bone or hard tissue, or ligaments; cure it with the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Parasitic abscess is a boil that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally in other places; and when it becomes swollen, and no attention is paid to it, if it grows, it will chase and run along the root of the nail, and possibly damage it entirely; and the corruption reaches up to the bone, until there is a foul-smelling pain, and the joints become wide and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When curing it as we have said in the previous section, and the cure does not help, then you must cut off the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is of great aid if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to swell, poke it with a hot iron, push it upwards, strike gently and delicately on the swollen area; then apply burning and corrosive medicines above it to remove all of it; afterwards heal it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 If the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw out pus, for as much as the bone becomes corrupt, it cannot heal; and if you see it becoming rotten, strike it with the spoon-like instrument as mentioned earlier, then heal it until it is healed; and if it is pierced and wounded, and causes great pain, it must be healed first; then cut the nail with a sharp spatumile from above, but do not let the cut reach the flesh below the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something over it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the injured hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 One should align the finger that is born in some man by chance to be entirely flesh; and sometimes there is a nail or bone there, and occasionally a nail grows from its root, or it originates at the knuckle joint of one of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The finger that is born at the base of a knuckle joint does not move, and if it is fleshly, its size is slight; cut off its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint should be treated carefully, cover him.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the finger that is born or should be at the end of a knuckle joint, it is necessary that you cut the flesh roundly up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and cure it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Simultaneously the swellings that come to the joints arise by birth, or by injury from a wound, or by burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If necessary, you should cauterize that wound so that it heals according to its natural shapes; then put between two thin fabrics or cloths dampened in oil of roses, so they do not stick together; or you may put between two pieces of subtle wood until the wound is healed as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If any of its bones come together with the palm, then strike the weld as needed.
des vils	 Of peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 The veins are large, swollen and full of melancholic superfluities which come to many members of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, rather than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purge of the gall, and then heal from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is to cauterize it and draw out black blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein and drain all the blood from it.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The thickness [of the tumor] is as follows: first, boil the leg in very hot water strongly until the flesh becomes softened, then hold the patient's leg above the knee up to the part below the kneecap; then cut open the vein at one of the three locations, in a large size; then separate and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can tolerate; and then tie it, and command the patient to eat meat that promotes bleeding; and start the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, which benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The swelling [of the tumor] is as follows: raise the patient's leg, if there is a lot of hair, then immerse it in water or put it in warm water, and boil the leg until it turns red and the veins swell; and if there is no water, heat it over the fire, and then cut near the vein along the long side of the thigh or at the bottom part below the knee; then peel off the skin with a knife, and expose the vein from both sides until it appears when felt; and it will appear red and black, and where it enters the skin resembles a white cord; then press down on it, making it swell under the skin, and then cut it at one end lightly, then in another place three fingers away; then peel off the skin over the vein again until it appears, then draw out the blood as before, and cut it at another notch as before; then make another incision, or more if needed; then draw it out, and when it is all drawn, press it; and if you cannot draw it out or lift it, put a very sharp double threaded needle into its entire length and pull it, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out; and be careful not to press, because if it presses, it cannot be pulled or lifted, which harms the patient; and when you have treated it all, put damp wool soaked in vinegar and oil on the wound site; and heal it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye is contracted, twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said, you must cut it open, but do not cover it; pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to pierce the eye should be curved and not cut through the vein; it should be thick because if it is too thin, it would pierce the vein. However, it should be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the common vein (civil vein)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein (civil vein) is found in the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground without moisture; however, it may appear elsewhere, which happens due to the corruption that comes beneath the skin, as it does within the body serpents and worms, piercing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the muscles change and the vein begins to forcefully emerge, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the joint is opened, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen from 7 to 10 inches long and sew it, leaving the linen on the leg, and every time it swells outward, you wrap around the linen and sew it; if it becomes too long, cut a part of it, wrap the remaining part, and do not cover its root, as long as it is completely emerged; for if you cover it, it returns into the flesh, causing an abscess and pus or poison and bad disease. Therefore, this should be treated little by little until the head is reached, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated is 5 or 10 fingers long, and once a man came to me whose vein was 10 fingers long. When you wrap around it, push it into a pouch or purse and pierce it all the way through, so that everything comes out; empty the matter inside it, and bring medicines against pus to the wound every day, then cure it as with an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes in opening this vein, hands get burned, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or hand, causing great injury and loss of fluid; heal it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called "cow disease" on our land because it often affects cattle, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body expanding and contracting, and is felt in one member to another until it reaches the skin or goes through it, and jumps out; it is caused by poison from certain humors, such as worms, snakes, serpents, and ascarides or roundworms in the stomach; it is doubtful about its malice, for when it travels through the body and reaches the head, it may enter the eye and destroy the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to cure and drain, one can force it out only when it moves: therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong rope tightly, then strike from above and draw it out, and if the end is full in the flesh and you do not pull it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it causes is that it burns oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold a bellows beneath it, then strike from above and draw it out; and it is necessary to use the patient with purifying of body medicines soluble for evil humors, and avoid sour foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 The pain arising from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is known as "vakirir" on our land and it is a pain that occurs in some members and moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and I found her arm swollen, and saw a small tumor in the armpit of the arm; afterwards, it began to rise like a worm towards the shoulder, faster than anything else, like live silver when it is cut from one piece; the pain separated from that place and entered the shoulder, and shortly after it ran throughout the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she returned again around the body as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease manifest itself in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 I wanted many to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, with open veins, and because of this appeared that constrained windiness; and they do not understand according to this reason by those who are ill and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, lay it above and below hastily, then strike on top so that the constrained windiness goes away from the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, cure it with those who expel the windiness, such as fetid pills or serapin pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	 arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse in their shapes and the parts of the body they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversity of them is such that there are those with large points and small, sharp or blunt, and serrated; and of those with two angles, and of those with tongues, and of those with pieces; and when one falls into any member it falls in accordance with two manners: either into a principal member like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidney, intestines, bladder, or similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it falls into any place of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterwards show up: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for many deaths come in different ways; and when this ill sign does not appear to you and the arrow is not fully embedded, pull it out and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the head swells which is above the brain, is also when scotomia (partial loss of vision) and blindness, and vertigo (dizziness) and redness in the eyes occur, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps without pain from the nose or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and swelling from the wound is white and resembling a boil, and it also swells as a bruise of flesh; and if this sign appears, refrain from treatment, and pull out the arrow if it isn't lodged.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.
