The sign of an arrow wound when it pierces the heart or body is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it has been driven into something hard, not hollow; and by chance the arrow may swell like a finger, and produces black cold blood, and chilliness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore it is known without doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never pierces the flesh is when there is no scum bubbling from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and seeks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls on the bedclothes, it is dislodged from the small ribs; and it releases great agony and pain and breathes heavily; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls or stomach, in case something of undigested meat jumps out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes or wounds the belly, and it does not burst through the intestinal path, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow strikes the bladder, and it bursts and leaks urine and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, like the hand and arm, neck, shoulder, and collarbone, spine of the back, ribs, pelvis, legs, and similar parts are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it's not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, do this instead.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow pierced or lodged in the root of his nose; I pulled it, and drew it out from below the fat of his ear, and he was saved without damage.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And I pulled out an arrow that lodged in the oil of the eye under the paper below, and the arrow was pointed, but could not be reached further than the point towards the skull, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, completely piercing both ears; the man was saved, and no evil accident happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears: I shaved the beards, and I softened it so much that I drew it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And I drew an arrow that was embedded either in the neck or abdomen of a man, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I incised on the arrow, manipulated it, and pulled it out, and there were no adverse effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 If a man has an arrow sticking out of his back or shoulder and the wound is sutured over it; and the arrow remains within him without changing its position or causing any problems in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And in another case, a man falls with an arrow in his body and the wound is sutured; and he endures for a long time without suffering great pain; and many similar things occur.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 The arrow strikes a man of the princes, who fell among the enemy and was slightly declining to the right side; and the arrow was entirely stuck for three days; then I was summoned to his treatment.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I pierced it with a very fine needle and did not feel it; but he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the tip of the arrow; I applied a healing plaster attractive and digestive because the wounds did not swell; and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I placed the plaster for many days, and healed the wound straightaway, and the patient stayed in this state for a long time until he felt the arrowhead within his body; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for many days, until it was opened, and tried it, and felt the tip of the arrowhead sticking out at the opening; then I inserted the medicine ague into the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and he lived more than four months, but afterwards the wound that I had sewn up burst open again in such a way that I could not pull it together with forceps; therefore, I did not stop trying and inventing ways to extract the arrow, until I made good forceps according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, as I drew it out and returned the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the mirrors judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and the wound was closed, and the patient was healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 And I have told you the quality of arrow extraction, that you place your care on what I am not saying, for the books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters comprehend little things and remedy what is present and failing, find nine solutions, and nine instruments, in the demise of foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs where they are inserted except in two ways: either by the side through which they enter, or from another side; and the one that jumps out from the side through which it enters is an arrow entering into flesh, and sometimes jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if the shoulder does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is swollen all around and the joint is made even; and likewise, if it has been thrust into the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for a few days and move it every day; then it will jump out, and if it does not jump, pierce it with a thin instrument everywhere until the flesh around it is opened up, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If the arrowhead is thrust into the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents I mentioned before occur: do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes even after a few days, for if the arrowhead comes loose, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not completely driven through but only into the bone and does not reach its target, and the patient remains ill for some days with bad condition, then consider extracting it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is driven in deep and cannot be withdrawn, administer tourniquets around it as I have told you; then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, then apply all your efforts to find it; if you can feel it, use any suitable tool to extract it; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, the deepness of the arrow, and no bone, nerve, or vein is present, widen the wound as much as possible; and then try to extract the arrow if you can, and if there are ears attached to the arrow like they hold on, remove the tissue that is lodged in its head from both sides as much as you can, and then either break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can extract it; but be careful not to break the arrow so that you can extract it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do so at once, if the wound around the arrowhead is opened, then draw it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood opposes you, bring what we have said in its chapter for treatment; and beware of incising the nerve or the vein, and use an instrument as much as possible to draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the shape they were when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do it, then do it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow coming from elsewhere, opening or anything related to it, or the skin is swollen around it, as one can see or feel evidently: cut then above, until pliers can grasp it, and then pull it out; if it jumps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held within the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone and expands the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot be extracted, leave it as it is, and then continue with the extraction until it comes forth; and if it is from an arrowhead, push it all the way out; and if it has fallen, and you see that a splinter has been administered, use an instrument with a pointed end, so that the point of the arrowhead enters the hair of the instrument; then push harder, and if the arrowhead is caught in the instrument, push the instrument with the pointed end entering further, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrowhead is touched, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if an arrow falls or pierces the belly, bladder, side or costal area and it is near, and you can cover it, then do so; be careful not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, then make the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many forms: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the hair tuft is also like the feather of a bird, to direct the point of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The forms of the tweezers for extracting and for measuring are as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	for wounds on the chest
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 From the veins that one drains are thirty-one, of which there is a head of sixteen, to wit: two batons behind the ears, which are called the "herbech"; and the two arteries in the temples visible; and the two veins that are in the hollows of the eyes, which are called "aspirators"; and the vein that is between the forehead; and the vein that is at the root of the nose; and the two glands that are on the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed in each arm are V: one is cephalic, which is on the left side and people call it "arm vein"; the other is called "fistula" and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and people call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is either on the right side, and people call it "vein of the stomach", which is above the elbow, and it is the one that is opened, revealing itself clearly above the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the superficial veins are the vein between the little finger and the ring finger, and there are two; and in the leg and foot, there are three: one is under the wrist on the left side, and the second is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nase" which is at the other ankle; and in the other leg, there are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The first hairs of the veins that are behind the ears aid the old cathartics and the emigraines; and the quality of the healer, as I tell you, is to grasp the head of the patient, and rub the place or the veins with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their proper places depending on the head: hold them there with your hand, and where you feel the pulse beneath your hand, press firmly; then take the lancet, and push it through the vein until the bone, then pull your whole hand upwards, cut and the skin and the vein well two times through, and make blood come out as you see; then hold it and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The drainage of the two arteries that are in the temples, this is suitable for treating old, soft, and recurring otitis, as well as weeping eyes; and the qualities of the draining are as follows: the patient should tilt his head, so that the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse below your thumb, then press it; then lift the skin on the vein upwards towards your thumb indicator, and push in the lancet, and lift the vein upward, and prick it, as you have done with other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and put your thumb over the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top of it; then form a knot and leave it until it is healed; we have previously spoken about their dressing and extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The opening of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the incision of the skull in ancient facial diseases, and it has migrated and turned red; and its qualities are that the patient tilts his neck while twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Place the point on the vein and press from above with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to its quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and never stop working with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the fire should not be too sharp; and it should pass through obliquely because the bone is close, and by chance break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The incision of the two veins that are in the eyes helps for healing, and for inflammation, redness, swelling, pain in the eye, and facial diseases; and the qualities of their incisions are that the patient tilts his neck while twisting with a rope, as before; then tie it up, and make the incision through the vein, a little bit long and wide because there is no skin.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the iron is thin, it may break; then make an incision for the blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The firstness of the vein's blood is beneficial against ague, and against pox and diseases caused by poison, such as migraines and redness that come from poison within the body, especially when it is old; and the qualities of the vein's blood are that the patient presses his neck, then holds his nose with your left hand, takes subtle long flame, and thrusts it into the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily, and the sand will start to flow soon; do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to necessity, then let it rest for a night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The first joint of the second finger helps in the setting of a fracture, at the beginning of swelling, and for many diseases, suppuration, rotting, herpes, and abscesses; and the quality of the joint is that the patient straightens their neck beneath one and the other, as we have said; and the master being on top of the patient, and the patient lies on the chair, then open the vein along its length a little widely, then draw blood moderately or as much as necessary; then do it again in another vein, then untie the ligature, and gently hold both veins so that the patient does not strain them; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the liver surgery
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sinuses of the veins in the upper lips help to drain into the mouth, and contribute to decay of the gums, fissures in the lips, and teeth problems and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the surgery are to make the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at the two veins, one on the right liver and the other on the left; they can be recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that there are smaller black veins around them: therefore grasp one and the other, and if you do not know which one is which or are uncertain, grasp the largest of each pair, and do the same for the veins above and below; this is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the liver underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The surgery of the veins that are underneath the tongue helps after head surgery and is done by cutting the throat; it treats diseases of the eye and diseases of the mouth; the qualities of surgery are: make the patient sit between your hands in the sun, hold the tongue, look under each side for a black vein; grasp one and the other but do not go too deep because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 Veins that are commonly healed follow two methods: either they are pricked with a pointed instrument made of hard material like iron or olive oil, and are called "anesil"; and they should be large and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mirrhin flame is very renowned, and it is large as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 It is necessary to open the large and visible veins that contain thick blood and are troubled, and this is the form of olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more finely, and it is for the fine veins to drain the subtle blood that contains yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps to heal diseases that are in the throat, neck, chest and abdomen; and it is necessary for the patient to be healed thoroughly and to avoid the artery that is beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if it touches the artery and bleeding occurs, it should be stopped, as I have said; but do not prick the flame, rather cut as with a lance.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilica does not open clearly, you must force it open and change another one; or you can apply any heat to it, or open the vein in the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with a lance at the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you want to know the place of the vein, then you must also force open the arm and feel for the pulse; then mark the spot where it is, tie the arm, and cut the vein with a lance; beware not to wound the artery when you see the vein swelling, because it is the artery: avoid that.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it rise up high, like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is not from an artery: then hurry, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when it stops bleeding, which happens often; tie the arm, and leave it like that, do not move it, let the patient not move it; be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the arm is not bled and it swells, and there is no medicine present, then cut open the artery if it is open, for the head of it will recede; bleed the arm.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a slice of fustic, cut it and take one half and bind it tightly until the next day; if it stops bleeding, that is good; if not, heal it as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow; and stopping the bleeding should not be ignored in various conditions due to the smallness of the wound and the pressure on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The first sentence of the text translates to: "The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and from the body below, as it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to pierce it along the nerve that is underneath. If he penetrates too deeply, and finds the nerve, it inflames and the patient becomes ill or injured, and there is a chance it will not heal; and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, it is necessary to open it with an instrument; and avoid touching the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 "The vein of the head also helps to drain blood from the head and assist the eyes; it is necessary to open it by piercing with olive oil or myrtle fire, for it is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Therefore, it is necessary to seek the easier joint, and not to worry if it needs to be done the first time, and then try again; and by chance some limbs swell in certain men when it needs to be done for the first time, but it should not be worrying.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the purity is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you need to know about bloodletting is that it should not be performed except to preserve health and avoid upcoming diseases; and it should be done in one of the three veins that are known: cephalic, saphenous, and basilic; and if bloodletting needs to be performed at the beginning of summer, during autumn, or winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The administration of medicine for diseases has no fixed hour, but it is necessary when required day or night, at all hours and in every moment; and it is not appropriate to administer medicine to children until they are 14 years old, nor to a woman bearing fruit until the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 When someone wishes to be administered medicine in any way, it is necessary that the intestines are cleansed with a light enema if there is much retained gas, so that the veins do not carry waste products to the main organs; nor should those who are overly salty with food or drunk, as long as they are in such a state, be administered medicine; and if one wishes to administer medicine after a colic attack, vomiting, abdominal pain, frequent urination, excessive labor, staying awake and fasting, and those suffering from poison or injury; then refine the humors, if he is not obese, by food and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so; then immerse in water, unless anything prevents it, to subtly purify the blood, and heal the vein from the third part as we have said; and keep that day from work, pain, lust, and similar things; and be bound and joyful, and let the healer stand higher than the one being treated, and rub the arm II or III times, then gently pull the ligament above moderately, for when it is too tight or narrow, it cannot heal without; then rub the area with both hands until the veins swell, and feel it; then moisten the healer's hand with a little old oil, then place his palm of his left hand under that vein where you wish to treat, so that the vein does not fail when being pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that behave like cords in a sieve, and some of these are filled with windiness, such that when you put the flame on them, they retreat from the flame, and cannot open the vein; this is one of those; and if the vein opens, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the people who do this should be careful about such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if (the patient) opens a vein the first time, that's good; if not, begin again under that place or immediately above it, if the vein is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 If the limb is swollen and the patient fears it, they should wait a day or two, and not bind the arm; perhaps abscesses will come out; do not enter with water, then start sieving again if it pleases you; and if the hole is small, or the opening is narrow, open it gently and subtly so that you doubt that no blood will flow out of it, but apply heat directly to the hole itself; and open it a little hastily, so that the limb is not swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the limb swelling, do not start draining it immediately, but put a little bit of oil on it, for the oil lightens the body with blood, and the oil is thickened in this place where the oil is applied; and thus administer the oil in each draining that you perform on the veins to stop the flow of blood; and this also stops triacle and bowel when applied to the limb; if it becomes too large, it becomes subtle and dissipates.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens when the opening of the vein is small, hurry up and put on the swollen limb a moist sponge in hot vinegar or oil for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains at the limb after several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not harm; and if you see it, put something made of aloes or myrrh, grated and mixed in oil of camphor, menthol, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often abscess and signs of the abscess appear in the sanctuary: therefore, put your hand on it, and if you feel the place soft when compressed by your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything above what we have said, for by chance in court without the artery; but make .i. a dry plaster to harden it, then cure it with another treatment until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it turns red; and if you see it swollen, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the one who is filled and swollen, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the veins be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and it must be drained little by little, and it should be drained by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of draining is safe from overflow of blood and compression of nerves, and is more useful than draining deeply rather than widely.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 To the one whose body needs to be drained, it is necessary to give moistened bread at the bottom of pomegranates; if he is warm, let him bleed three or four times. And for those of cold constitution, eat moistened bread in syrup or honey aromatic syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cumin, and a pleasant smelling syrup before draining.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if it (the patient) has a wound at the thigh, after the evacuation of much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth made of charcoal, and fragrant subtle syrup, and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to burst open one of the arms and heal it again at times, if it is weakened by repeated bleeding, then let it heal little by little, according to the amount of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if you want to burst open one arm after the first bleeding and it has a strong chest, then let it heal for 6 hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if you want to heal from another part, it should be healed on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For much blood has leaked from the body, which causes fever; in such cases, it is necessary to draw out a large quantity and widen the wound as wide as possible; then you should follow all the conditions of treatment for wounds, and place your hand above the pulses when it bleeds, so that death does not occur at the site of bleeding, which happens often when the healers are negligent; and it is not good to dislocate the arm and draw blood again if the wound closes, you should press firmly instead; nor if it is curved, extend the arm quickly, but leave it until it bleeds a second time; or you should touch the tip of the flame at the opening of the vein, so that the coagulated blood from the vein comes out and place a piece of fresh linen on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is open, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess has been pacified.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If you need to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are connected to the vein of the head because they are composed of them.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of the wounding is that the patient pushes their hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red; then it should be bound gently, so that the vein appears clearly, then it should be pierced thinly, neither wide nor long; and it should be cut wide open, and it should be cauterized well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be done, the hand should be put back into hot water, and let the blood flow out in the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not pound the hand into hot water again, for it puts more winter than summer into it; and the cauterization of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The hot cautery of the thumb should be applied to all liver diseases, and this is how it is done: hold the thumb, apply hot sharp, until the vein has fled if you can see it; and if the wound is transverse, and if you cover it entirely with everything, it will cause no harm; do not go too deep, because the nerves are completely exposed under all skin, then put the thumb in hot water again, provided that the wound is not frozen over and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as necessary, put oil and wax on top of the vein to quickly seal it, and do the same with each one (vein).
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood from the left hand is useful for the sickness of paralysis, and do it as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The cautery of the vein should be applied to all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the spleen, dropsy, kidney stones, and old leg or thigh ailments, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the qualities of its healing are that the patient should place their foot in hot water and scrub over the vein until it perishes, and tie it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from below the foot it goes very deep; therefore heal where the largest vein, or at the ankle, is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you let the blood flow from above the foot, beware of the veins that are below it, and let the blood flow through as when cutting; let the flame be quiet.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the bone cannot come out, put the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 If the healing is required for the first time, start again a little higher since it is salted; do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and similarly treat the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The large vein of the sciatic nerve is at the shin bone, and its pain resembles that of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the qualities of its healing are that the patient immerses it or bathes and strains above the ankle four fingers while turning, for otherwise it does not open; and if it opens, heal in all ways that you can, and crosswise; and it is more effective to cut it, for the leach is full of it and it is much responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you do not set it right, there is no remedy for the one whose back or side hurts in the small of the waist, and beware of the nerves; and make as much pressure on the blood as you can see, then untie the ligament, and put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of the sores from boils
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and blistering is done in two ways: either by drawing blood or without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cautery called ventosation, which is for injury, is of two kinds: either it is general, or specific; and the ventosation made by injury and extraction of blood is performed in 14 parts of the body, from which one is entirely in the head; and the others are in the neck; and the others in the two sides of the neck; and the ventousations under the jaw; and the ventousations of the two shoulders; and the ventousations on the hips; and the ventousations in the two arms; and the ventousations in the two legs; and the ventousations in the two ankles; and the ventosation does not treat blood, unless it is small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it should not be done at all, unless it is done like venesection of a vein; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from congestion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if it is necessary due to illness to apply leeches or for customary reasons, let us administer them once every hour at the beginning of the month or at its end, and both in between and at each time; for there are some who, when they have need to apply leeches, have a heavy head; and there are some who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head and neck, and their eyes are clouded; and there are some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen, and they ooze blood; and if there are such people, they think, and see dark spots and hallucinate and die and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, and especially during the month [of menstruation], we order to bleed after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The application of leeches to the nose helps with headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not advisable to do this after the evacuation of the entire body; and this leeching is in place of cephalic bleeding, and it should not be used for those who are cold in constitution or who have a running nose, as it does them great harm; and therefore neither the sick nor those with cold head diseases should use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And whoever heals themselves often become forgetful, and because of this it is necessary to place the leech (a tool used for bloodletting) a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is in place of the windpipe near the base of the skull, and for this reason it is beneficial for compression of the throat, splitting of the channel of the voice box, and strangulation; and it must be pressed gently, because if it holds too tightly, it may cause injury to the throat or the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation on the chest of the neck causes pain in the head, toothache and migraines, strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth; it is in place of the windpipe of the basilica; you must instruct the patient to press his hand in order to make it, not to press an artery, and not for blood to flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations beneath the chin are useful for treating mouth disease and corruption of gums, as well as similar diseases in the mouth; they are located near the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations of the shoulders are useful for treating disease caused by heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the costal veins are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; instruct the lord not to prick too deeply, for the muscles are naked of flesh and know beneath black and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse that is on the buttocks is effective for emordes from the root and for diseases beneath it, and it should be large and made of iron, as it needs to be well drawn; and in case it is too thin, it would break; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses of the legs heal open wounds, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are effective for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and remove pus; and they are in the place of the thighs and ankles, and in all cases they weaken the body over a long period, and bring phlegm in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the bladder (ventouse) is such that you first empty it, then fill it immediately and apply it hastily, move it equally, and not stop doing so until you see the place turn red and swell, and appear the redness of blood; then press and remove the bladders, and pay attention to the position of the body, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: you must pierce only once, and must make wide incisions, and a little deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If the wound is large, you must pierce it twice: the first time to refine the blood vessel's path.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very thick, you must pierce it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we should only do so once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 If we wish to draw a large amount of blood, we should often pay it back; if the vein is thick, prick too deeply, and let the wound be closed quickly, and for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and narrow pores, you should anoint the muscles of the ventosation with stimulating and dissolving oil: if in summer, use violet oil or sweet almond oil or oil from cucumber seeds; and if in winter, use oil of parsley, lily, camomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take bitter almond oil or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the patient whose wound you are treating has tender flesh and large, open pores, do not put any oil on it, but rather wash it after ventosation with rose water, cold water, mulberry water, cucumber water, porcelain water, or other similar solutions.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from asafetida or marjoram and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with large superfluities should rise from old wine, or juice of sour grapes, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and do not fumigate before the bath nor bathe, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after ventosation, and it is necessary that he evacuates when he should be ventosed and when he has been ventosed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And watch out for the one who is recovering and is colicky, and he lacks sharpness and is inflamed excessively; then it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuces, and similar things; eat little, consume chicken broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And if the person has a cold complexion, take honey syrup and fragrant wine that is neither old nor new, eat little, consume poultry and small birds and sparrows; on the day he vomits, he should drink more than eat; it is also necessary to give some men certain times triacetum or muscatel before or after the vomiting, to comfort the main organs; and let the weak ones be made subtle, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The following harnesses that are placed to wound are those that are placed on the liver, the spleen, gout, stomach and the buttock and the flank and the thigh and the loins, for these members do not endure being wounded otherwise, and it is done only to draw blood from one member to another, as we put on nipples when they are sore; to remove the viscosity of a member, as we put harnesses on the stomach and the flank to reduce swelling; and to relieve pain, when there is obstruction or a stone, it relieves by its attractive power accidentally the obstruction, or moves the stone from its place; and so does it when placed on the liver and the spleen when there is retention of wind, and these harnesses are administered empty for only sucking; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way one fills the harness with hot salty water or with water in which herbs such as coriander have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister to be administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers and a half of breadth and palm's depth, and have a small hole around the middle similar to pushing an awl, and it should be made of iron, soft enough in front so as not to prick the patient when placed on the limb; and there should be a rod of iron or steel across the middle for applying a splint, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the wounds of children are different from those of the old, and thin from thick.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this splint should be placed on the limb: take the linen or wax and place it inside the hole in the rod that is within the splint, so that the light does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and the fingers should be over the hole as we have said, so that when one sees, if steam goes out, one removes the splint; then take the linen again as before, and repeat often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder which is administered in pleurisy disease, it has no worm nor ulcer, and it is not brought forth unless when it is full of fluid, and it is placed on the member only; and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without bladders are brought forth only in members where a bladder cannot be placed due to its small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in areas deprived of flesh, such as the back or neck, and other similar areas; and the quality of the liquid is that when you find bladders which are in sweet clear urine without any putrefaction, you take them; and place one in sweet warm water until they become familiar and have nothing in their bellies; and then it should be incised with a vein and a bladder, then rub the member till it becomes red, and place the bladders on it; and when they are filled and hot, if it is a place where a bladder can be placed, place it there, for it is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the shoulder blade from below, then above, very carefully, and press it back into place; and if the shoulder blades are too close together along the body of the ribs, moisten a linen cloth with cold water, put it on, until the ribs have desiccated; and if the ribs multiply, put vitriol powder or similar things on until they have desiccated; or you put half peeled fava beans on the shoulder blade, and leave them until they harden to the shoulder blade, which will now stop the bleeding; and if there is more need for it, take other ribs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the ribs do not want to take, rub the shoulder blade with fresh blood or you prick it with a needle until the ribs bleed, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they harden; and when you see that they are leaking, sprinkle some powder of aloe and flax or charcoal, which will now stop the bleeding.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the repair of fractures and dislocations.
