Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Inform the dear child that the foolish man should flee from this chapter, for he will never find any ancient books or read letters in them; and because of this, knowledge is foreign to our land, for I have never found good knowledge on it, nor do I know anything about it except through the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the subject, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained within, and abridged it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of instruments that are presented, as I have done in these two chapters beforehand.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who have been proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When bruise or dislocation or twisting or curvature comes to anyone, it is necessary that you quickly clean the patient on both sides, unless something stops you from doing so such as weakness of body, old age, or infancy; or if the time is not very hot, or too cold; and consume cold meats, for example raw fish and mutton's eye and shin, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill yourself too much with foods that fill veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscess heating or the spreading of matter to the member; then the patient will return to his first proper care.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that cause thickening, or those that are viscous like cooked wheat in water and meat, and beef, and mutton, and veal, and fish, and fresh eggs, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For more frequent and quick healing of the bones, it is represented that nourishment is needed.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that the broken bones of the old and weak cannot be well recovered or repaired according to their nature due to the relaxation of the limbs; neither can those who are too tender, as bones of small children; but there is no remedy, set the broken bone above with large splints which hold the limb together until it enforces itself as it was before; and do not let it touch at all its work, and for this reason feed it with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all the ways of break in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to a tree, and another while sharpening, as the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, then it is a small fracture.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And at each time have your tool, and the proper equipment in restoration according to what memory comes to its place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone is by this that the joint is twisted, and wide open due to displacement, and compressed with the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting nor touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have twisting or splitting or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with your hand, but put on the medicine that comes after this, and then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fractures that go to the branch, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now align them equally, so that abscesses do not grow there; and if abscesses grow, let it be for a certain amount of time until the abscess is calmed; then align it with the bone as easily and wisely as possible, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration where there are pieces; then hold, as necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 If there are broken pieces in the bone, whether it is a hand or foot, or a small member, or with two cords, or one cord and your hand; then arrange the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you reduce all additions to their joints as necessary, and ensure that through your work, no injury or pain comes to the patient; then align the two bones well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems not to be well aligned: straighten it nicely, and do not strain or press it too much, nor make it hot and contracted like those who bring about abscesses and contractions in the member by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limbs are set, well bind the patient so that he does not move, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and be careful that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For if it feels no pain, it is not set, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain; be careful that it is set straight, for crookedness should not come when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs can be in various sizes and shapes.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members such as the arms and thighs: if you wrap them with soft and fine linen cloth; and for the large ones like hips and legs: you should wrap them with a wide and strong cord, since the wide cords hold the whole large member equally, and they tighten it all evenly, so that there is no swelling; then tie light bands around it three or four times according to the member, and tighten your hand slightly on the entire cord, then go to the top of the break and tighten less, than the break, and move the break a little; and soften the cord little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another cord, and turn it around the broken limb in the opposite direction; then return to the underside of the break, and tighten moderately, neither too strong nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above; then put linen or cloth strips between the cords, until they are all even, then tie everything over with a bandage, and then put well-made stays on, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is an abscess or boil, place a warm, soothing substance on it and let it stay for some days; then press firmly with your elbows, using a stick about half the thickness of a large cane or a fust used for splitting logs, or a palm-sized reed, as in this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 It is necessary that the elbows placed on the injury should be slightly larger and longer than the others; and should also be as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large; then press firmly with the elbows in the same way as you did in the first line, then tie above it a thread coming from the left, as in the first line on the injury; it should be narrower, then wider; and it is necessary that the thread should not be too thick nor too thin, and should be made of flax; for if the thread is too thick, such as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their knots from twisted flax threads, and this is a great error, because the knot cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each elbow.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient has been struck by the heads of arrows in the shoulders after being reset, place linen or wool padding under them so they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is broken and the bone is shattered, I will explain the remedy below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind all broken limbs immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limbs are large, you should not put hot irons on them before five or seven days, or more according to your confidence in the abscess healing; and here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour that is kept near the mill walls, mix it with an abundance of egg, and make this mixture neither too clear nor too thick, and apply it, and this is the common method of restoring a fracture in various ways, and especially for women and small children, as it is not too hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for restoring breaks, dislocations and twists: take aloe, linden, elder, asafetida, arabic gum and myrrh, all in equal parts; add aloeswood and mix with plenty of egg; if the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, as it has a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones to their place, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of plaster for twists: take mugwort and vismalve, mix in ten parts; mirrh and aloes, mix in nine parts; acacia bark six parts; bolech of Armenia ten parts, grind well, mix with vinegar or an abundance of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of splinting for joints and dislocated bones, easing the pain that arises, and shaping it with the bone, and breaking: take new linen, wet it in water and oil, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This splint does not heal, but it is good for easing abscess heat and bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for plaster that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground ivy, grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of splinting for the healing of broken bones and for hastening the healing of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, crushed beech leaves, and of each one an equal part; grind together with wine, and if the limbs are scalded, use it with moist coriander water or vinegar.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of compression stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of mallow, flax, balm, clover, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and camomile, in equal parts; grind and concoct with salt water, sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that no other substance should be put on a broken limb to restore it except for a plaster made of wax and oil, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it appears Galen says one should place dry, warm things on the broken limb to heal, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another remedy for injury and pain: take the mugwort plant and crushed human hair or bird feathers, and egg yolk, all evenly ground, and make a plaster with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then loosen slightly later on, and make sure the patient feels no pain, nor has the bones moved from their place; if it is not loosened for many days and pain comes to the place, or swelling, without rest or healing, hasten, and loosen, and remove the compression now; take a light cloth, sea sponge moistened, dip in water, wring out the place until the itching ceases, and ease the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry linen, wet with water or rose oil, and tie on top of a nut, until you are sure the abscess is hot; and let the inflammation of the member rest, and the pain be removed, then continue the gentle binding, and a little compression, and not too strongly as before; and bind gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is swollen and red and painful and inflamed, and you need to open it up and bind it, then repeat the process as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no swelling comes to the limb as we have said, you should not release it before three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes you leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the break heals, and approaches the joint with the flesh; then hold it more tightly than before, and make the flesh thicker, as I have said before; and if you see that it dries out too much, know that nourishment cannot enter there; then give warm hot oil, every day, and slightly moisten the area; by this method you cut off the nourishment from the limb, and hastily correct what fools do who leave the member twisted: this is harmful, and it is a dangerous operation, and I see nothing but laziness and working improperly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many types of fractures exist, and they have diverse shapes; for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, causing the bones to break completely from the collar bone up to the shaft below the bone, as is done by a halberd or mace; this type of fracture is called "haichure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above piercing through, and this type of fracture is called 'complete'; and this is the break in the two types of bones, whether large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow from the side, a crack or a cut by a stone, falling on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent break, which approaches the membrane that lies beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if the wound is healed into the bone as fine as hair and has a small fissure, it is called this type of fracture "capillaire"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone or falling, or something similar, causing a piece of the bone to enter below, and the joints are crushed as a blacksmith when hammering over pots; if a splinter goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more often in those who have moist bone in their head, such as an infant's skull; and it occurs in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are dislodged, like splinters; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We should know all the ways of breakage by traction over them, and the inquiry with probing, and the corruption of the flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy resemblance is known by this: when the bone is exposed and scraped over it, if the break is blackened, it appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, take care of the patient's conditions; and if you see any bad signs such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, paleness, high fever, hairs growing and turning red, or other signs in different positions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any uncertain signs, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the splinter first comes to you, and it is in winter, it should be removed before the fourteenth moon (which is about 28 days).
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is corrupted, and the complications mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 If the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane covering the brain, then you must split the broken part in this way: take the head of the patient and expose the bone on all sides as much as possible; over the shape of the wound make it softer than possible, and if drainage of blood or pus comes out to expose the bone, or abscesses filled with pus, use whatever is necessary, and fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the abscesses are calm, and make sure there is no more drainage; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut obliquely in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, sharp and made with iron instruments; and work lightly, so as not to cut the main part.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is forced and hard, then you must pierce it around, in such a way that you provide measurements with tapers, not making them so thick that they penetrate beyond the bone's edge, and above the point it should have a margin or circle, which doesn't allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you should have more than one, so each comes at the correct location on the bone's edge, so you have tapers for all sides; and this is the form of the four kinds of tapers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one taper on the bone and turn your hand until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the taper slightly aside, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the fracture lines as subtly and lightly as possible, so that you draw the bone to your hand or any of the instruments that you have such as pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the pressure which remains of the bone to all other similar instruments, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other instruments; and if any small bones or scales remain, do not leave them, remove them gently with the tools; then treat the wound with pincers and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of work is the one that Galen mentioned, which is more sure; and he praised it much, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone where the fracture opens up; so that when you have exposed this part, place beneath it the head of this incisor chisel, as shown in its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 Do not cut it from one side only and let the parts be jagged in two edges, so that the saw is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, so that you split the bone lightly all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath; if it is pressed against the bone, remove it gently, for it can be split senselessly and out of fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through to the cloth, and the bone is only cracked from above, and there are small pieces, then one should smooth it out afterwards, and remove the scales with a sharp rasp of various sizes, in order to provide the most suitable amount in each place, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king [or leader] shaves his head closely first, then afterward with something more subtle, and does not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other kind of haircut and breakage, it is necessary that you bring about the result according to his discretion; and this is not something that can be answered by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the wound is open, you should take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound and soak it in rose oil, then place it on the wound; afterwards, take another cloth doubled over 2 or 3 times, soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible to not burden the wound, then administer more linen over it but do not tighten it more than necessary to only cover the wound; leave it like that for a day or two until the abscess subsides, then remove it and administer medicines such as root of lettuce, flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and put it on the wound, and immediately administer trustworthy medicines without bitterness; be careful that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment or pus on it, for when pus accumulates on the linen covering, it rots and may cause great harm to the patient; for when something bitter is placed on the wound, it corrodes from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no unfortunate accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful with great uncertainty.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness (gangrene) comes violently except through medicine that we have put on it, for which reason it has this virtue, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in linseed oil, and spread it on the wound; then cure it in ways of treating wounds until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one alone because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but instead causes swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 If one of the two parts is broken, you must bite your little finger or thumbnail, and put the fracture inside your index finger, and at the nail edge, until the nail grows again according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the breakage is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach it, you must insert a small stick into the nostril up to the root.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If the fracture is of one part, then do the same, and hurry to restore it within a day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then press at the tip of the nail with linen cloths, if the fracture is in one place.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Tie two threads of opposite parts, if the fracture is there; and let the threads be as thick as they fill the pores of the needle.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said any remedy that one must moisten the tents with butter, and churn each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It seems not to be good, but they should be moistened in the mixture of egg white and flour; then leave the tendon until the bone is hard and the cartilages are toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of goose are inserted in place of tendons, and if one layer of linen is around it, and the breakage is held, then blow the patient gently through it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess comes to the opening as you are working on it, put beeswax or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of alum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If abscesses do not open, apply an ointment externally, made of flour from the sisamend plant and incense powder mixed with egg white; then put light dressings on it and do not bind it too tightly; if the break in the neck is small and broken into many pieces, remove it with suitable tools; then sew up the wound, and treat it with substances that promote healing and mending, such as ointments and liniments; and if there is no wound within the neck, treat the tendon, and put planks of cane on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated below, and there is no wound outside, and only the break is visible, but it has not been broken in two, if one knows it easily, then it is recognizable as a corbel inside.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, place your index finger in the patient's mouth; if the break is on the left mandible, place your right index finger from outside and push it gently inside, and align it with the other hand from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the mandible is displaced at two points, then you must administer an extension of two parts until it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or fracture, hold them with a gold, silver or silk thread, then place a broken-baked mandible on top, and put on one double cloth; and place on the cloth a large and well-made stitch, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and attach it where you can, and command the patient to rest, and give him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see the figure change (dislocate), dislocate it again on the third day, then reset it where it was dislocated; apply a plaster of milled powder with egg or flour of wheat, after removing the broken bone; and put on the plaster a light linen, and if the plaster sets and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals; many times it heals in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And when an abscess comes, bring what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, be careful not to remove any piece of the bone when extracting it; use tools suitable for this purpose with caution.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, widen it as necessary with fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces, if none remain, then sew up the wound, if it is wide, and apply one or more suitable dressing for healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the arm
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force is broken many times towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated at two places, divided into parts, and is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the fracture is without wound, you shall have two helpers, so that one holds the shoulder where the force is broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then align the fracture to your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and has neither appearance nor deviation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to stretch more, place a round bandage of cloth or linen around the patient's shoulder and make it thick as needed; then stretch and bind the force, and pull the bandage tight with your hand, aligning the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the dislocation from its enclosure because it comes in fully, then the patient should lie on his affected side, and put a small pillow under his shoulder; and push the ministers (assistants) the shoulder downward until the bones of the dislocation are raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find that it is broken, then it is necessary that you cut through it; and draw apart the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot join due to any hindrance, strike one of the incisions that you have made; but place this instrument under the dislocation to keep it in place:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it seems like a spoon, and is not concave, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the effort; and let there be two concavities, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, as the groove of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are assured of the incision being deep enough, cut the wound, and if the groove is small, or you doubt the incision is deep enough, use linen and tweezers, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if pus comes from the abscess heat, then soak a linen cloth in rose oil, wormwood and wine, and put it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The binding of the bone, when there are wounds and cuts, is to put the plaster of mill powder and egg yolk on the bone, and place light stoppers on top, and put a splint under it if necessary; then take a very wide bandage, about one palm wide, then cover the stoppers with two layers of linen, and the plaster; then take a thin stick of three feet long and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging; and place the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the patient's armpit, and under the patient's arm if possible; and tighten each part, and when you see that the ends meet properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, you should check it every day, and when the linen loosens, you should tighten it; put the patient on their back, and place a small pillow under the armpit to lift the shoulder, this will align the fracture of the shoulder blade by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad circumstances occur, until twenty days have passed; then reapply the plaster if necessary, and tighten and leave it in place until it is healed; and it is healed the most in twenty-eight days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates wide from its place, and it can only be felt with touch; if it appears according to the shape of the break, and you reset it according to its natural form in all ways possible; then sprinkle powder from the mill over it with plenty of egg whites and light strains, and put a double cloth over it; then put a wide and delicate stick on top, about a little larger than the shoulder, and if there are any protrusions in any part of the shoulder, use linen strains to even out the stick so that it fits evenly; then tighten it all with a great band firmly, so that the stick does not move from its place, and watch the ligament every day; and whenever it softens, tighten it, and make the stick equal if it is away from its place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days, And when this number is complete, loosen it, and be careful, for it is not bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes in front and not beneath the skin, raise it up, and cut the bone, and do as we have said in the treatment of an abscess to cool the heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture with this method
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The limb is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens seldom; however, it often breaks near the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken from the inside, it slips downwards, and the patient experiences great pain, lack of alignment, and immediate bleeding, and the wound opens in the broken bone, and he feels it all very much.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on their back, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides to your hands, and carefully align it in all ways possible, so that the bone figure is as required; then place poultices and pouches filled with salt or another light substance on top of the broken bone, wrap it in one cloth, and attach it to the broken bone so that it does not move; then turn the limb round and round, and tighten it gradually, and check every hour whether the fracture has healed, and if it softens, tighten it again; and if it is necessary to dislocate it, due to corrosion or inflammation that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, you hasten, and dislocate it, remove the poultice, and direct those who have come for treatment; then reattach the poultice, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in large ones after the back and at the chest, and they bend only when they are slippery; and it is felt well by the examination of the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the resetting is that you set the fracture straight as needed.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then place a splint and bind it with a stick if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the broken rib is tilted inside, the patient feels intense pain and shortness of breath, like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces it; and he goes to points, and quickly vomits a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and they have used great ingenuity for it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the broken bone outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot compresses come, if they have not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, let them be applied.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And it was said by some that vents are placed on the wound to drain pus, and this seems reasonable; however, doubt exists whether the vents attract superfluous matter to the wound due to its weakened state.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some said that the wound should be covered with damp linen dipped in hot oil and a tourniquet placed between the ribs to make it even; then it should be cured with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because the fractured bone is not covered by a cloth and he doubts himself, then you must cut above the level of the broken rib, and place an instrument under it to hold it; then you should carefully split the bone apart, remove the broken ends, and sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with splints until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when an abscess comes, place soft wool soaked in rose oil on top of it; and hold the place that needs to be treated in position; and let it rest on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there comes a fracture of the bones in the neck, and so it happens with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 If it happens to someone and you want to know if it will heal or not, if you see his hands softened, swollen, and dead, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they feel nothing.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in various positions, and if it does not move or feel when they are stretched and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient should be cured, if care is taken.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing comes to the spine in the back, and you want to know if it is hollow or not, take care if the feet are numb, and if the accidents that occur are in hands, and above the back there is sudden movement without control; and when it has been brought up onto the stomach, it jumps and there is sudden movement without control.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is pushed up onto the back and you want to sit down, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is deadly; do not treat it at all.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen to them, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you anoint it if there is an abscess burning, place oil of rosemary or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then put a comforting and drying plaster on top, bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, you should cover it with some oil; cut the bone, then join the two edges of the wound together with stitches if it is large, then heal it with healing ointment for as long as it is well; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow," you should put your left thumb in its place and make it equal to the right hand, then apply a plaster and bandage on top if necessary; then bind it, and if there is any dislocation, correct it; and heal the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the leg bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it does happen, there is only slight reduction in pain at the site; it lasts for a long time, declines towards the opening, causes pain and swelling at the location where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break; and feel which is the break and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, then equalize that break so it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or it declines inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach so that the restoration of that break can be done.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it (the dislocation) straight, place the plaster on top, then place a stick or a splint over it, and hold the break still so that it does not move; and apply the joint underneath the ribs until the fracture is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess should burst, do not touch it until the abscess has healed, and place what we have previously mentioned on it; then return to the treatment, hold it as needed if there is no bad accident, and that's the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the chest and the neck of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: of which one is that you take a rod filled with coarse linen, in this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two limbs and the splints together with two ropes, and suspend them above; then place the patient on a chair; then lay the broken arm on the rod, until it reaches the correct position, and have a small amount of rod in between; then suspend it to a heavy object or the assistant holds it downward; then the healer puts the break in the correct position with both hands together, until the break returns as necessary.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that they restrain the patient on their bed, and tie the hand to the neck, then command two attendants that one presses where it is broken with their hands, and the other presses all around completely, and extend each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you think the extraction is more difficult, hold the ligament beneath the break, and above the break, and stretch each of the assistants to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you must place the middle splint under the shoulder blade and the other towards the break; and if the fracture is towards the shoulder blade, then place a light splint gently, without labor, until the break is equal on the surface, and on the shoulder blade; then make the break equal, as necessary, and hold it in place, unless abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess comes out, do not hold it for more than seven hours, and put a soft cloth soaked in oil and linen on it until the abscess is calmed; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you place the cestui (the instrument) on the break, then raise the arm toward the shoulder or chest; and tie the bandage and hold it on the shoulder and arm so that the arm is in a straight line, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint above the fracture, with one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it spans the fracture two inches from each side; then hold the splints in position, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, firmly and less in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 If you see the position of the shinbone and its straightening during the repair of a broken limb, as we have said, and you doubt an abscess has formed, then leave it bound for seven days, as we have said; then examine every three days the binding, to ensure no inflammation arises at the site, or pus comes to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if such an accident does not occur, it should not be dislocated except after three or more days, and the patient should sleep on his back and keep his hands on his stomach; and place a bandage of linen under the shoulder joint, equally thick, and observe every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or the ligaments are not softened; if the direction is regained by the power of medicine, and food that has been mentioned before is given to him, in such a way that the meat is first made subtle; and when it begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be set right in 40 days; and then it must be dislocated again and a bath and ointments for realignment administered.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the structure is deformed and swollen, it remains to dislocate for days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius", of which one is small, and this one forms the little finger; and the other is large, and this one is below, near the little finger joint; sometimes only the larger ulna bone breaks, or only the smaller radius bone, and sometimes both.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small fractures are broken, the restoration is easy, and healing; but when large ones are broken, healing is poor, and more difficult than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small fracture that is broken, it should be slightly extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large fracture, it should be strengthened more strongly; and extend above the splint, and place the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the others, and cross the patient over himself, and the splint in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the ministers arm under to the part below his hand, or elbow, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the surgeon should set it (the shoulder) even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken in pieces, put each part back into its place, and if none of them can be properly set, cut off the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking there is an open wound, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; take care of the wound.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if at the beginning of the reset there are pus-filled abscesses, glue a cloth made from rosin and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; place the cloth over it gently, until the abscesses have been soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 Then remove the rosin, and apply a plaster of milled powder with egg white, then place the splints, and let the splint from the fracture be stronger and a little larger than the others; and know that it should have six or more splints in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more on the fracture than elsewhere, and less when moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are over the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the thread, with which it is tied, be made of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And hold the limb and the joint afterwards for some days.
