Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as pruritis that comes to the limb, then you should irrigate the limb with hot water until the itch is soothed; and let the limb not be left to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Then resume the bandaging, and if the joints are crushed and the bones dislocated, and similar things, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the narrowing of the orifices cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, then you must soften it a little, and let it be for some days until the narrowing passes, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not remove the bandages for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 What is moreover around, then he will place his hands on his neck, and let his neck be even, and keep it from movement and from bending, and sleep on his back; know that this break will be restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and the complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The fracture at the back of the hand and the fingers happens rarely, but it often occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient should lie with his back straight and evenly on the ground; then place his hand on a cloth stretched out, and the attendant should extend the broken bones and align them with mirrors so they are well joined; apply the plaster and bandages if an abscess does not form, then insert a splint according to the size of the fracture, and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the side of the palm near the abdomen, make a splint from cloths and instruct the patient to strap it to his fractured hand; then bind it with a long cloth, and make the splint as wide as the palm of the hand, and tighten it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the edge, it should be that you place a splint above, and another below in the heel, so that the hand remains open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and bandage the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in any of the fingers, whether it is the thumb, it should be equalized as needed; and hold with the heel, and if you see that you place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not let it move; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, equalize it, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together in one place, for movement is worthless, or place a splint on top, such as a thumb; and take care in the healing and positioning of the abscess, and treat what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	broken ankle
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and it is clearly seen when it twists forward and backward; and the restoration is as follows: one ligament above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his ligament equally to its place; and this is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, it is one of the ligaments towards the knee, and the other ligaments below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is close to the knee, then it is the ligaments below the knee and the extension below; then place the mirrors on the bone equal to its two hands, as it should be according to its natural figure, and then place the splint and the strap, unless an abscess does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool down first, then return to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 You must wrap above the fracture with a bandage doubled in two or three layers, and remove any excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the neck, and thread the long string between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the ends of the string above; then turn the leg and the bandage upwards, then place the straps on the fracture and a strap on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to straighten the strain, then begin to tie three or four times around the fracture; and as you move further away from the fracture, and less constrain it; then go back to the two strings that you have threaded between the leg and the thigh, and tie three straps that are above, then return below to the ends of the string, until you reach the foot; and constrain it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, unless an abscess or inflammation or any similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a fracture, straighten it and align what comes out, as we have said many times; if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they should be cut off if possible; if not, the area should be broken and the fragments removed; treat it as we have said until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way as if iron stakes are inserted into it, just like the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration, this does not alarm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the thigh is restored within one day, or a little more or less, according to the various complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin area
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint occurs little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not a fracture, but rather a crack or piercing, and there is pain at all wounds and injury, and the patient feels pain greatly.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes that which is rounded at its joints until it can be moved assembled; then place the splint, and put in a round peg, if you need it, and tighten it as needed, then check all the arrangements we have said in other breaks, such as abscesses, boils, and other similar ones; put at each accident that which is needed for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called correctly "mouse" [tibia], and the other is called "shinbone" [fibula]; and it breaks similarly to the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is equal to that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 If the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it can be seen; and it twists under itself.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply extension and make it equal, and bind the joints equally; but in case the break is ugly, and there are more pieces, the extension should be less and lighter; and align it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two fists full of straw that will brace the leg on one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in a knot so that the leg cannot tilt to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should administer one bandage of straw for the length of the leg, and it should be tied together, and the leg will be immobilized for movement, and properly made at the break where there is injury; move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident; heal it until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no breakage, but the bones of the foot sometimes have a break and the toes may be broken, and there is no fear but they are crushed in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bone of the foot, and you see one bone rise above the other, then place the patient on his back as if he wanted to walk, and then place your foot on the patient's stomach where the bones are elevated, and press as much as necessary until they return to their places; then place a splint and padding on it, and place a small board with two flat cups under the affected foot, then pull the bandages around it, and do other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after four or five days have passed, undo the bandage, for you will find the bones aligned, either fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if either of the bones is fractured, restore it as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the fractured bone according to its length, and it should be slightly wider; then place under it the board that I mentioned, and pull it towards the fracture site; and if there are two or more fractures, break them, placing a splint on each fracture, wrapped in one linen cloth, and secure the board under the foot; and ensure that the top of the board is facing the abdomen of the foot, covering it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have said; and treat each accident according to its need.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the bone of the female pelvis is broken, make it swell with large pieces, then incline it towards the lower back and hold it from behind; fill the hollow of the female with cloth of the patient's linen, as thick as a stone; then turn the woman, lift her buttocks little by little, and pull out the cloth until it reaches the entrance of the bone, and the bone returns with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cloth, and when she has finished, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the fracture will be healed, and if you see, take a bladder of burdock, tie one end of a cord to it, and blow all the bladder into the bone; then blow strongly through the cord so that the bladder inflates inside: the bone will return to its place; then fill with cloth, and leave it for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone at the elbow of the man is broken, either that of a woman, restore it as we have said in the hinge-bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and skill into them and heeds my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For fracture means in many ways the right way of restoration; therefore, pay attention.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the arm, when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and insert the arm into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with an open wound, whether it is large or not, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or similar, that it should be set now, as the testimonies of the healings that we have mentioned show.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, then apply vitriol to it, if you have nothing else; then begin to set the fracture in that same hour, or continue on that day, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses arise, wait until the ninth day, allowing them to be pacified, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about a bad event.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears exposed at the surface of the wound, it should be set gently with light pressure and in a slightly extended position.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the tendons are not prepared for setting in an equal position to your hands, you must align it with this tool made of iron, which is 7 or 8 inches long and the width is according to the size of the wound; therefore, the mirror should grasp 3 or 4 fingers, according to what is needed in each bone-setting procedure; and let it be round and somewhat large so that it does not bend under pressure on the member during your work, and sharp at the front and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "hainche", which means that the curved shoulders should be placed on top of the visible part of the bone; push it once until it returns and make them even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must cut the visible part of the bone so that the instrument has control.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, within your power; then remove that which is immobile in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Keep it in its place, then moisten the linen cloth with black styptic wine, and apply it properly if it is hot; do not put any oiled plaster or other substance on the wound that may cause decay and corruption; then administer stirrup bandages when you have set the bone, leave the wound uncovered, and cover it with a layer of linen cloth according to the size of the wound, taking care that the wound is not constricted by the break; and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, and they have caused pain or death or decay for the patient; and the bandaging should be softer and more pliable than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain at the place, do not put on tourniquets; but wrap around it instead, in place of tourniquets, hard bandages, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And after a day or two, if the wound begins to swell again, remove what you have put on it and apply healing salves for wounds, such as tetraformula and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be set straight in this manner so that the bones are aligned lightly downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but instead bows back, since there are small pieces of bone, therefore you must try to open the wound and remove all the loose pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula or any other form of corruption comes to the place, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he said in this chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And if the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thighbone or shoulder blade, or similar major bones, do not drain it, for often death comes from this, but let it remain until it can heal; perhaps it will harden by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving bruises on the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Often times after the breaking of health, especially near the joint, it is a horrible sight to see the figure of the limb; and by chance, the limb cannot perform its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then of yourself: if we are to administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocola, acacia, and similar others, in such a way that you take one of these things or all together and crush them with sharp wine or with vinegar or egg white; and put it on the sore in poultices, and press it well, and do not remove it for many days; then you dislocate it, and repeat another, as long as the nodulation is removed; or you strain over a piece of plank well made; because the property of the plank is that it removes all swellings from the limbs. And if the nodation has already become hard like stone, and it needs to be removed, you chop it off, and make the superfluity apparent; or you shave it with a sharp razor, as long as it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after care
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored and remains after the members are weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: one of them being that it was tied too tightly and not as needed; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nutrients could not reach the member; or due to excessive arrows; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and make the body become thin, until the blood multiplies in him; then administer a bath, and give him joy and pleasure; afterwards put ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts great nutrients to it, and the sore often gets hot with cold water, until the nutrients reach the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration and the bones broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless its natural function does not perish; do not believe the foolish who say one must break the limb anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and it brings great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and tortures are fresh, then they should be soothed with hot water or softening herbs such as comfrey leaves, radishes, medicks, and similar things; also, make a poultice of mollifying medicines such as daqiu, and take musk from the comfrey plant, mix it with gum elm or sesame oil, and apply a poultice; or you may take ripe figs, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that alleviate pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes, the dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and longingly with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is growing and hardening, as stone, it requires to be cauterized, it should be covered up to the bone, making a subtle incision gently; and place moss and cotton in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it is now necessary to return it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if you wait, the joint swells, and in case it is reset at the joint; therefore, do not move it until it has subsided: many times it causes spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, let the patient bleed, then leave it alone until the abscesses have calmed down; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently rotate it, and treat each limb as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the neck down to the feet.
des mandibules	The jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It sometimes happens that the jaws are dislocated from their places, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: either they are somewhat disjointed from their places and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, and causing the saliva to flow out of the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns by various means.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is whole and complete, you must quickly reset it, without delay; and in this way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and pushes the thumb of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand should be spread out, to make them equal; and command the patient to soften, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the hand is made even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return, it is the same if it is both lower jaws together, you anoint them with hot water and oil, until they are easily reset; do not rush to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are reset equally, and the mouth of the patient closes well, put on soft moistened cloths made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with several bands; let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders should be between two cushions so that he moves neither to the right nor to the left, nor forces himself in any way, but takes light food until the pains are removed, and the jaws are numb; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not strain at all opening the mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaws are numb and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be set right again within an hour and are not returned to their places, fever and common sweats come, and possibly abdominal rupture, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction; and many times he who experiences this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the collarbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate inside the ribcage due to continuity and pain, and it is occasionally dislocated outward, and this is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms; then presses the shoulder firmly with your palm, and it will return; then put on the splint and bind it; and the shoulder which is towards the neck cannot dislocate; if it does, and if it dislocates once, reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the splint and bind it again, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way, the shoulders of the back are reset when they are dislocated from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the part of the socket below; the second is at the part of the hip; and accidentally dislocates above, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside the nerves; and often dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for it jumps out quickly; but in those who have enough flesh, it jumps out slightly and returns slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, a blow or fracture occurs, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must verify it, as long as you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocation when it goes down towards the socket, there is a difference between the sick and healthy shoulder, and you will find between them a manifest difference; and at the top of the shoulder, you will find a hollow, and below the socket at the touch of the top of the shoulder, as if it were an eye; and the sick cannot bring their hand to its place, nor make any movements; and similarly, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not only difficult to correct when it is new, unless the infant is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister raises the patient's hand high, then places his palms underneath it, and forces the joint upwards to its place; and the minister raises the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it down; it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in many days, the patient should be bathed in hot water; and bring a soothing and calming remedy such as a concoction of althea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and bring it; then lie the patient on his back, and place a piece of linen equal to the shoulder under the affected one, not too soft nor too hard, then place the foot of another on the linen, and lift the head of the shoulder carefully, pulling the hand of the patient; and have another minister hold the head of the patient so it does not move downwards; that shoulder immediately returns, and if you see it dislocate again in this way: it is necessary for a person larger than the patient to be present; he should be upright facing the side, and push the affected shoulder under the patient's shoulder, lifting the patient's shoulder upward so the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the patient's hand downwards towards his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, he cannot bear anything heavy with him, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And one also performs it in another way: and it is when one thrusts the long thorn into the ground, so that the head of the shoulder is as round as a pea, and not too thick or too thin; then it should be placed beneath the patient but with wool underneath, and the patient should lie lengthwise on the staff; then the hand should be extended towards the other side in shape, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, one performs this cure: take a thorn from two strong branches and four fingers wide, which has a sharp point at the end to enter fully under the buttock, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the patient on the bed with a soft pillow beneath, so as not to hurt him, then place the patient's shoulder under the patient's armpit; extend one arm above the post, and hold the dislocated shoulder above the post, and the arm near the wrist to the patient's head, then place another arm on one side of a broad beam of a door, and let the hands hang down below, and leave the body hanging from the other side; the joint will then be put back in place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner that may be, you must put an equal-sized cloth under the armpit, then sprinkle the splint prepared with mill powder, along with incense and egg yolk, all over the shoulder and around it, then tighten the bandage under the armpit accordingly, and twist the cord over the splint, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be fed a little amount of food, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then feed more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it remains firm and does not become soft, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or for another reason, then you must administer fire cautery at three places, as it is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not stay in place and cannot lift the arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either compressed or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the hip, and the buttocks or backside, is caused by impact and stretching of hands, and another treatment may be applied; and care should be taken until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing of the member comes swelling, and it moves slowly, then let the patient use baths many times, until that swelling subsides, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	The cost of dislocation is...
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the dislocation of joints costs [to] be dislocated at points, and it costs [to] return to its place; and if it has been dislocated from all sides, and both before and behind, and the dislocations are not repaired because it is clearly seen and felt; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the healthy bone with the diseased one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is swollen and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder completely.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset [the dislocation] thus when abscesses come, for if abscesses come, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be set back into place entirely, especially when it is at the rear; it is worth more than other dislocations, and it is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes there.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that you stretch out your hand to your two hands; and the arms should be spread out, and the hands should be placed on the mirror according to the outline around it, above and below, and push the joint to its sockets or root of the palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it will return when you fold your hand over your hand and push from the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and this is done by two people who extend the arm, and two others who strain it so that it does not move at extension; then turn the arm on each side, once you have wrapped a double-length and wide cloth around it; and when the eye joins the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is in its place, apply dry plaster with egg yolk and strain it, and keep the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for a few days, then unbind it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is in its place, break the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the manipulation and the ligament, and leave it like this for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if it causes pain after the joint is reset, and it swells, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed; or you place a sheep's wool fat on the jointure, then leave it for a day and a night, then take it off, and let him enter the bath; and when it sweats, wipe the jointure gently, then put the wool back on, and then enter the bath again; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, place warm moistened hay covered with butter and press it on; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the wrist is light, more so than other joints; it should be returned to its place quickly, immediately when it is dislocated, unless the limb is swollen or there is hot abscess nearby.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the reset position should be that you place the diseased hand on a table, and stretch out the assistant's hand, and align it with the patient's, so that the palm is even with the appearance of the jointure, and push until it returns completely; it is necessary that you watch if it is well in its place; then have the patient put the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's back of his hand on the table, and have him position his hand above the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, that's good; if not, apply pressure with warm poultices to the abscess, and let it rest until it begins to heal.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot tolerate it and you cannot set it in place after some days, the dislocated joint remains twisted; this does not harm the patient as long as his hand is disabled and cannot grasp anything: therefore know that the nerves or arteries are severed, or there is no other means of help except for setting it with a fire cautery, and by chance, nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, place the plaster that we have said upon it, then press and leave for five days, then release and leave so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well and there is no swelling, wet with hot water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers on the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on either side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then press the dislocation towards your chest until it returns, then hold the finger's head and turn it toward the separated part; leave it for two days, then make it equal on that day; and wrap it tightly, as we have said, and unwrap it daily, move it and align it; do this often, until it is straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly side of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and do the same when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	for the dislocation of the vertebrae of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebrae of the back or neck are dislocated, if there is no cure for it, then death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that the excretions jump without volition, cannot be held, and many times soften any member, or the two knees or the two arms or the neck; and many times the spine becomes silent at four parts; the one which becomes silent in the back is called "gilbositez": treatment is that you consider whether the gilbositez has come from childhood: if it has not healed or been cured at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cure used great words, but it is not beneficial in all cases; however, I have shortened it according to my intention and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes before, there is neither trick nor health; and similarly the one that comes straight in two sides, and cannot be cured except for him specifically who comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient should lie on his face in one place, and have pressure underneath him, so he does not bleed; then insert the needle into the main hole in the ground, and the other at the feet, and tie a loop over the patient's body, and the other at the knees, and at the thighs, and at the ankles; and two attendants know the loops, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two needles; and they should be well closed, the needles as we have said, and the assistants place their palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if the dislocation does not return by this cure, take a board three arms long and curved at one end, place the patient on their side, and push the head of the board under the opening, then put the middle of the board on the spine; place the mirror's feet on the other head of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with the pulley that turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And take two needles, one arm long each, and between each needle, have a palm's length of space; and in each needle, have the pulley that turns, and let the needles be firmly in the ground so they do not move; and between the two needles have the turning needle, like the cables turn, and to turn the pulley have two small needles of a palm's length, to turn the pulley; then tie the rope that is among the straps to the pulley towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other pulley, and each of the attendants turns his pulley along the entire rope, and the master adjusts the spine equally as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is evened (the shoulder), place a dessicative plaster with much egg, then bandage, and then apply the stick of a tablets three feet long, which should bring out the joint and the healthy part of the spine, then tie with a rope as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nursing until it is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing, you must administer soothing medicines, with the stick as mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes the appearance appears at the back spine of the shoulder, and one believes that it is a dislocation; but this is the bone that opens, for which you should not have any presumption, because perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the shoulder dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Note that dislocations of the shoulder and the joints of the arm only come from dislocations, and not in other joints; and the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in four ways: inside and outside, front and back; more on the inside, and less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation within is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer and opens wider the sick thighs than the healthy ones; and the sick person cannot bend their knees in fire; and it is the joint that is dislocated and swollen with abscesses that becomes hot, because the head of the calf goes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens to swell, is that this incident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him whose leg is swollen, are that it is straight according to the completion; however, it does not double at the knee due to pain, and if you wish to make it walk, it cannot do so beforehand, and it retains its urine, and when he walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him whose back hurts, are that he cannot stretch his knee or bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the hip is located under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The corrections for this type of dislocation are as follows: examine if the dislocation is old and remains in its position without treatment; and there should be no presumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case of fresh dislocation, which is of four types of dislocations, you should act quickly by turning the joint and pushing it inward and outward, and move it left and right; if it returns, it will not need any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must summon a strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie it to something above the knee; another minister extends his hand thus, so that he pushes his hands under the thighs, then tightens a rope ligament above the calf; another holds the head of the ligament; and all extend upwards and downwards at once, until the patient is raised from the ground at once and hangs.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common for the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If the shoulder is not in place, you must provide care to its condition. When the dislocation is at the front, you should remember to have the patient lie on their affected side, then tie a cord around the thigh's root, and the limb that is under the angle. Then tie the cord upwards towards the angle and toward the joint; then take another helper and grasp the large limb of the affected thigh, and stretch it out backward. It will return to its place now; and this method for dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 If you cannot secure it in the manner we have said, then you must bind both of the patient's feet tightly with a strong cord above their heels and knees, and the affected leg should be extended two fingers longer than the other; then hang the patient from a pole suspended above the ground, with their arms hanging down long. Then command one of the helpers to grasp the top of the thigh, and let another helper hold on with the patient, who will grasp the thigh in shape, for the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is at the front, the patient lies down, as we have said in those who have gout, and pulls the ligament above the sick leg properly, and also above the hip; then place two iron rods, one at the head and one at the feet, then pierce the rod between the thighs into the patient in the desired shape; and place damp cloths around it to prevent the patient from bleeding, then extend each minister towards him, and the mirror holds the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place him on a bed and press as we have said in the case of gout, and the patient lies on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg as quickly as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the hand on the sick angle, then press with the other hand, and move it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is at the back, it is not necessary to extend the patient's leg downwards, nor lift him up off the ground, but rather he should be positioned like when a woman is dislocated at the back, as we have said in the lying on two beds; and let his face be upward, and the legs extended as we have said before, and press him hard on the joint towards the table; and when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then adjust the knees, and put a pillow, and tie them with a bandage so that the leg does not move; and rest for three or four days, then release it, and place a pillow on it; and if you see that they are equal, tie as before, and leave for three days; then release, and let him walk well until the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee joint is dislocated in three ways: inside and outward, behind; do not dislocate it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull apart between your hands, then bend both sides of the knee joint; another attendant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that it bends lightly to the knee; and apply ointment, and bind the leg to the thigh, and leave them together tightly for three or four days, then release; and do not let the patient walk, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not set (broken), administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the fracture, until it heals.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes crushed, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 The signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and try to push it back to the part where it is displaced: the repositioning should be gentle, and it must be gently extended by hand when it has been reduced only.
