Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, then lift it up, and push the foot up strongly; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, lie the patient on his back on the ground, and drive the passeil (a tool used to reduce a dislocation) firmly into the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around it so that it does not hurt the patient; then hold the leg of the minister, and another minister stretches the foot at the hand or at the ankle, keeping it above the foot; then each minister holds it evenly, and the passeil should be in place between the thighs of the patient to keep him when it is set; then place the mirrors evenly on the dislocation with their hands, and another minister holds the leg straight below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is in place, put the plaster and woolen bandage on top, tighten it, and attach the foot to the leg, watch the nerves that are above the ankle so that the ligament is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligament softens, tighten it again; then release it on the third or fourth day, and let the patient walk for four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess has come, it is necessary that you appease it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	The two (hands/arms)
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the limbs are dislocated, they must be very carefully extended without any effort, and it is an easy matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any way out of place with respect to the foot, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or table straight up, and put your foot under the joint that opens, then press your foot firmly until it returns; when it is even and there is no opening, put a two-fingered table under the foot's heel, then tighten it, and leave it for three days, then release it; let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and it is to be restored, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment, if you are not wise in the art or have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor hasty; and first apply soothing things to the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of healing; but when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place as soon as the soothing agents arrive; and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing things to the abscess, and treat the wound as necessary, drying it with cautery; and if the dislocation has caused a fracture and small bones are displaced, break them and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of entering into fear, according to what I have said, because this is according to your Creator, and because of the wisdom of your weapon and body.
Amen	 Amen (Amen)
